3141         /**
3142          * Produces a method handle giving read access to a reflected field.
3143          * The type of the method handle will have a return type of the field's
3144          * value type.
3145          * If the field is {@code static}, the method handle will take no arguments.
3146          * Otherwise, its single argument will be the instance containing
3147          * the field.
3148          * If the {@code Field} object's {@code accessible} flag is not set,
3149          * access checking is performed immediately on behalf of the lookup class.
3150          * <p>
3151          * If the field is static, and
3152          * if the returned method handle is invoked, the field's class will
3153          * be initialized, if it has not already been initialized.
3154          * @param f the reflected field
3155          * @return a method handle which can load values from the reflected field
3156          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails
3157          * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
3158          */
3159         public MethodHandle unreflectGetter(Field f) throws IllegalAccessException {
3160             return unreflectField(f, false);
3161         }
3162 
3163         /**
3164          * Produces a method handle giving write access to a reflected field.
3165          * The type of the method handle will have a void return type.
3166          * If the field is {@code static}, the method handle will take a single
3167          * argument, of the field's value type, the value to be stored.
3168          * Otherwise, the two arguments will be the instance containing
3169          * the field, and the value to be stored.
3170          * If the {@code Field} object's {@code accessible} flag is not set,
3171          * access checking is performed immediately on behalf of the lookup class.
3172          * <p>
3173          * If the field is {@code final}, write access will not be
3174          * allowed and access checking will fail, except under certain
3175          * narrow circumstances documented for {@link Field#set Field.set}.
3176          * A method handle is returned only if a corresponding call to
3177          * the {@code Field} object's {@code set} method could return
3178          * normally.  In particular, fields which are both {@code static}
3179          * and {@code final} may never be set.
3180          * <p>
3181          * If the field is {@code static}, and
3182          * if the returned method handle is invoked, the field's class will
3183          * be initialized, if it has not already been initialized.
3184          * @param f the reflected field
3185          * @return a method handle which can store values into the reflected field
3186          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails,
3187          *         or if the field is {@code final} and write access
3188          *         is not enabled on the {@code Field} object
3189          * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
3190          */
3191         public MethodHandle unreflectSetter(Field f) throws IllegalAccessException {
3192             return unreflectField(f, true);
3193         }
3194 
3195         private MethodHandle unreflectField(Field f, boolean isSetter) throws IllegalAccessException {
3196             MemberName field = new MemberName(f, isSetter);
3197             if (isSetter && field.isFinal()) {
3198                 if (field.isStatic()) {
3199                     throw field.makeAccessException("static final field has no write access", this);
3200                 } else if (field.getDeclaringClass().isHidden()){
3201                     throw field.makeAccessException("final field in a hidden class has no write access", this);
3202                 }
3203             }
3204             assert(isSetter
3205                     ? MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsSetter(field.getReferenceKind())
3206                     : MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsGetter(field.getReferenceKind()));
3207             @SuppressWarnings("deprecation")
3208             Lookup lookup = f.isAccessible() ? IMPL_LOOKUP : this;
3209             return lookup.getDirectFieldNoSecurityManager(field.getReferenceKind(), f.getDeclaringClass(), field);
3210         }
3211 
3212         /**
3213          * Produces a VarHandle giving access to a reflected field {@code f}
3214          * of type {@code T} declared in a class of type {@code R}.
3215          * The VarHandle's variable type is {@code T}.
3216          * If the field is non-static the VarHandle has one coordinate type,
3217          * {@code R}.  Otherwise, the field is static, and the VarHandle has no
3218          * coordinate types.
3219          * <p>
3220          * Access checking is performed immediately on behalf of the lookup
3221          * class, regardless of the value of the field's {@code accessible}
3222          * flag.
3223          * <p>
3224          * If the field is static, and if the returned VarHandle is operated
3225          * on, the field's declaring class will be initialized, if it has not
3226          * already been initialized.
3227          * <p>
3228          * Certain access modes of the returned VarHandle are unsupported under
3229          * the following conditions:
3230          * <ul>
3231          * <li>if the field is declared {@code final}, then the write, atomic
3232          *     update, numeric atomic update, and bitwise atomic update access
3233          *     modes are unsupported.
3234          * <li>if the field type is anything other than {@code byte},
3235          *     {@code short}, {@code char}, {@code int}, {@code long},
3236          *     {@code float}, or {@code double} then numeric atomic update
3237          *     access modes are unsupported.
3238          * <li>if the field type is anything other than {@code boolean},
3239          *     {@code byte}, {@code short}, {@code char}, {@code int} or
3240          *     {@code long} then bitwise atomic update access modes are
3241          *     unsupported.
3242          * </ul>
3243          * <p>
3244          * If the field is declared {@code volatile} then the returned VarHandle
3245          * will override access to the field (effectively ignore the
3246          * {@code volatile} declaration) in accordance to its specified
3247          * access modes.
3248          * <p>
3249          * If the field type is {@code float} or {@code double} then numeric
3250          * and atomic update access modes compare values using their bitwise
3251          * representation (see {@link Float#floatToRawIntBits} and
3252          * {@link Double#doubleToRawLongBits}, respectively).
3253          * @apiNote
3254          * Bitwise comparison of {@code float} values or {@code double} values,
3255          * as performed by the numeric and atomic update access modes, differ
3256          * from the primitive {@code ==} operator and the {@link Float#equals}
3257          * and {@link Double#equals} methods, specifically with respect to
3258          * comparing NaN values or comparing {@code -0.0} with {@code +0.0}.
3259          * Care should be taken when performing a compare and set or a compare
3260          * and exchange operation with such values since the operation may
3261          * unexpectedly fail.
3262          * There are many possible NaN values that are considered to be
3263          * {@code NaN} in Java, although no IEEE 754 floating-point operation
3264          * provided by Java can distinguish between them.  Operation failure can
3265          * occur if the expected or witness value is a NaN value and it is
3266          * transformed (perhaps in a platform specific manner) into another NaN
3267          * value, and thus has a different bitwise representation (see
3268          * {@link Float#intBitsToFloat} or {@link Double#longBitsToDouble} for more
3269          * details).
3270          * The values {@code -0.0} and {@code +0.0} have different bitwise
3271          * representations but are considered equal when using the primitive
3272          * {@code ==} operator.  Operation failure can occur if, for example, a
3273          * numeric algorithm computes an expected value to be say {@code -0.0}
3274          * and previously computed the witness value to be say {@code +0.0}.
3275          * @param f the reflected field, with a field of type {@code T}, and
3276          * a declaring class of type {@code R}
3277          * @return a VarHandle giving access to non-static fields or a static
3278          * field
3279          * @throws IllegalAccessException if access checking fails
3280          * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
3281          * @since 9
3282          */
3283         public VarHandle unreflectVarHandle(Field f) throws IllegalAccessException {
3284             MemberName getField = new MemberName(f, false);
3285             MemberName putField = new MemberName(f, true);
3286             return getFieldVarHandleNoSecurityManager(getField.getReferenceKind(), putField.getReferenceKind(),
3287                                                       f.getDeclaringClass(), getField, putField);
3288         }
3289 
3290         /**
3291          * Cracks a <a href="MethodHandleInfo.html#directmh">direct method handle</a>
3292          * created by this lookup object or a similar one.
3293          * Security and access checks are performed to ensure that this lookup object
3294          * is capable of reproducing the target method handle.
3295          * This means that the cracking may fail if target is a direct method handle
3296          * but was created by an unrelated lookup object.
3297          * This can happen if the method handle is <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#callsens">caller sensitive</a>
3298          * and was created by a lookup object for a different class.
3299          * @param target a direct method handle to crack into symbolic reference components
3300          * @return a symbolic reference which can be used to reconstruct this method handle from this lookup object
3301          * @throws    SecurityException if a security manager is present and it
3302          *                              <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">refuses access</a>
3303          * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the target is not a direct method handle or if access checking fails
3304          * @throws    NullPointerException if the target is {@code null}
3305          * @see MethodHandleInfo
3306          * @since 1.8
3307          */
3308         public MethodHandleInfo revealDirect(MethodHandle target) {
3309             MemberName member = target.internalMemberName();
3310             if (member == null || (!member.isResolved() &&
3311                                    !member.isMethodHandleInvoke() &&
3312                                    !member.isVarHandleMethodInvoke()))
3313                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("not a direct method handle");
3314             Class<?> defc = member.getDeclaringClass();
3315             byte refKind = member.getReferenceKind();
3316             assert(MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsValid(refKind));
3317             if (refKind == REF_invokeSpecial && !target.isInvokeSpecial())
3318                 // Devirtualized method invocation is usually formally virtual.
3319                 // To avoid creating extra MemberName objects for this common case,
3320                 // we encode this extra degree of freedom using MH.isInvokeSpecial.
3321                 refKind = REF_invokeVirtual;
3322             if (refKind == REF_invokeVirtual && defc.isInterface())
3323                 // Symbolic reference is through interface but resolves to Object method (toString, etc.)
3324                 refKind = REF_invokeInterface;
3325             // Check SM permissions and member access before cracking.
3326             try {
3327                 checkAccess(refKind, defc, member);
3328                 checkSecurityManager(defc, member);
3329             } catch (IllegalAccessException ex) {
3330                 throw new IllegalArgumentException(ex);
3331             }
3332             if (allowedModes != TRUSTED && member.isCallerSensitive()) {
3333                 Class<?> callerClass = target.internalCallerClass();
3334                 if (!hasFullPrivilegeAccess() || callerClass != lookupClass())
3335                     throw new IllegalArgumentException("method handle is caller sensitive: "+callerClass);
3336             }
3337             // Produce the handle to the results.
3338             return new InfoFromMemberName(this, member, refKind);
3339         }
3340 
3341         /// Helper methods, all package-private.
3342 
3343         MemberName resolveOrFail(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, String name, Class<?> type) throws NoSuchFieldException, IllegalAccessException {
3344             checkSymbolicClass(refc);  // do this before attempting to resolve
3345             Objects.requireNonNull(name);
3346             Objects.requireNonNull(type);
3347             return IMPL_NAMES.resolveOrFail(refKind, new MemberName(refc, name, type, refKind), lookupClassOrNull(),
3348                                             NoSuchFieldException.class);
3349         }
3350 
3351         MemberName resolveOrFail(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, String name, MethodType type) throws NoSuchMethodException, IllegalAccessException {
3352             checkSymbolicClass(refc);  // do this before attempting to resolve
3353             Objects.requireNonNull(name);
3354             Objects.requireNonNull(type);
3355             checkMethodName(refKind, name);  // NPE check on name
3356             return IMPL_NAMES.resolveOrFail(refKind, new MemberName(refc, name, type, refKind), lookupClassOrNull(),
3357                                             NoSuchMethodException.class);
3358         }
3359 
3360         MemberName resolveOrFail(byte refKind, MemberName member) throws ReflectiveOperationException {
3361             checkSymbolicClass(member.getDeclaringClass());  // do this before attempting to resolve
3362             Objects.requireNonNull(member.getName());
3363             Objects.requireNonNull(member.getType());
3364             return IMPL_NAMES.resolveOrFail(refKind, member, lookupClassOrNull(),
3365                                             ReflectiveOperationException.class);
3366         }
3367 
3368         MemberName resolveOrNull(byte refKind, MemberName member) {
3369             // do this before attempting to resolve
3370             if (!isClassAccessible(member.getDeclaringClass())) {
3371                 return null;
3372             }
3373             Objects.requireNonNull(member.getName());
3374             Objects.requireNonNull(member.getType());
3375             return IMPL_NAMES.resolveOrNull(refKind, member, lookupClassOrNull());
3376         }
3377 
3378         void checkSymbolicClass(Class<?> refc) throws IllegalAccessException {
3379             if (!isClassAccessible(refc)) {
3380                 throw new MemberName(refc).makeAccessException("symbolic reference class is not accessible", this);
3381             }
3382         }
3383 
3384         boolean isClassAccessible(Class<?> refc) {
3385             Objects.requireNonNull(refc);
3386             Class<?> caller = lookupClassOrNull();
3387             return caller == null || VerifyAccess.isClassAccessible(refc, caller, prevLookupClass, allowedModes);
3388         }
3389 
3390         /** Check name for an illegal leading "&lt;" character. */
3391         void checkMethodName(byte refKind, String name) throws NoSuchMethodException {
3392             // "<init>" can only be invoked via invokespecial or it's a static init factory
3393             if (name.startsWith("<") && refKind != REF_newInvokeSpecial &&
3394                     !(refKind == REF_invokeStatic && name.equals("<init>"))) {
3395                     throw new NoSuchMethodException("illegal method name: " + name);
3396             }
3397         }
3398 

3399         /**
3400          * Find my trustable caller class if m is a caller sensitive method.
3401          * If this lookup object has full privilege access, then the caller class is the lookupClass.
3402          * Otherwise, if m is caller-sensitive, throw IllegalAccessException.
3403          */
3404         Lookup findBoundCallerLookup(MemberName m) throws IllegalAccessException {
3405             if (MethodHandleNatives.isCallerSensitive(m) && !hasFullPrivilegeAccess()) {
3406                 // Only lookups with full privilege access are allowed to resolve caller-sensitive methods
3407                 throw new IllegalAccessException("Attempt to lookup caller-sensitive method using restricted lookup object");
3408             }
3409             return this;
3410         }
3411 
3412         /**
3413          * Returns {@code true} if this lookup has {@code PRIVATE} and {@code MODULE} access.
3414          * @return {@code true} if this lookup has {@code PRIVATE} and {@code MODULE} access.
3415          *
3416          * @deprecated This method was originally designed to test {@code PRIVATE} access
3417          * that implies full privilege access but {@code MODULE} access has since become
3418          * independent of {@code PRIVATE} access.  It is recommended to call
3419          * {@link #hasFullPrivilegeAccess()} instead.
3420          * @since 9
3421          */
3422         @Deprecated(since="14")
3423         public boolean hasPrivateAccess() {
3424             return hasFullPrivilegeAccess();
3425         }
3426 
3427         /**
3428          * Returns {@code true} if this lookup has <em>full privilege access</em>,
3429          * i.e. {@code PRIVATE} and {@code MODULE} access.
3430          * A {@code Lookup} object must have full privilege access in order to
3431          * access all members that are allowed to the {@linkplain #lookupClass() lookup class}.
3432          *
3433          * @return {@code true} if this lookup has full privilege access.
3434          * @since 14
3435          * @see <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#privacc">private and module access</a>
3436          */
3437         public boolean hasFullPrivilegeAccess() {
3438             return (allowedModes & (PRIVATE|MODULE)) == (PRIVATE|MODULE);
3439         }
3440 
3441         /**
3442          * Perform necessary <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">access checks</a>.
3443          * Determines a trustable caller class to compare with refc, the symbolic reference class.
3444          * If this lookup object has full privilege access, then the caller class is the lookupClass.
3445          */
3446         void checkSecurityManager(Class<?> refc, MemberName m) {
3447             if (allowedModes == TRUSTED)  return;
3448 
3449             SecurityManager smgr = System.getSecurityManager();
3450             if (smgr == null)  return;
3451 
3452             // Step 1:
3453             boolean fullPowerLookup = hasFullPrivilegeAccess();
3454             if (!fullPowerLookup ||
3455                 !VerifyAccess.classLoaderIsAncestor(lookupClass, refc)) {
3456                 ReflectUtil.checkPackageAccess(refc);
3457             }
3458 
3459             if (m == null) {  // findClass or accessClass
3460                 // Step 2b:
3461                 if (!fullPowerLookup) {
3462                     smgr.checkPermission(SecurityConstants.GET_CLASSLOADER_PERMISSION);
3463                 }
3464                 return;
3465             }
3466 
3467             // Step 2a:
3468             if (m.isPublic()) return;
3469             if (!fullPowerLookup) {
3470                 smgr.checkPermission(SecurityConstants.CHECK_MEMBER_ACCESS_PERMISSION);
3471             }
3472 
3473             // Step 3:
3474             Class<?> defc = m.getDeclaringClass();
3475             if (!fullPowerLookup && defc != refc) {
3476                 ReflectUtil.checkPackageAccess(defc);
3477             }
3478         }
3479 
3480         void checkMethod(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName m) throws IllegalAccessException {
3481             boolean wantStatic = (refKind == REF_invokeStatic);
3482             String message;
3483             if (m.isObjectConstructor())
3484                 message = "expected a method, not a constructor";
3485             else if (!m.isMethod())
3486                 message = "expected a method";
3487             else if (wantStatic != m.isStatic())
3488                 message = wantStatic ? "expected a static method" : "expected a non-static method";
3489             else
3490                 { checkAccess(refKind, refc, m); return; }
3491             throw m.makeAccessException(message, this);
3492         }
3493 
3494         void checkField(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName m) throws IllegalAccessException {
3495             boolean wantStatic = !MethodHandleNatives.refKindHasReceiver(refKind);
3496             String message;
3497             if (wantStatic != m.isStatic())
3498                 message = wantStatic ? "expected a static field" : "expected a non-static field";
3499             else
3500                 { checkAccess(refKind, refc, m); return; }
3501             throw m.makeAccessException(message, this);
3502         }
3503 
3504         /** Check public/protected/private bits on the symbolic reference class and its member. */
3505         void checkAccess(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName m) throws IllegalAccessException {
3506             assert(m.referenceKindIsConsistentWith(refKind) &&
3507                    MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsValid(refKind) &&
3508                    (MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsField(refKind) == m.isField()));
3509             int allowedModes = this.allowedModes;
3510             if (allowedModes == TRUSTED)  return;
3511             int mods = m.getModifiers();
3512             if (Modifier.isProtected(mods) &&
3513                     refKind == REF_invokeVirtual &&
3514                     m.getDeclaringClass() == Object.class &&
3515                     m.getName().equals("clone") &&
3516                     refc.isArray()) {
3517                 // The JVM does this hack also.
3518                 // (See ClassVerifier::verify_invoke_instructions
3519                 // and LinkResolver::check_method_accessability.)
3520                 // Because the JVM does not allow separate methods on array types,
3521                 // there is no separate method for int[].clone.
3522                 // All arrays simply inherit Object.clone.
3523                 // But for access checking logic, we make Object.clone
3524                 // (normally protected) appear to be public.
3525                 // Later on, when the DirectMethodHandle is created,
3526                 // its leading argument will be restricted to the
3527                 // requested array type.
3528                 // N.B. The return type is not adjusted, because
3529                 // that is *not* the bytecode behavior.
3530                 mods ^= Modifier.PROTECTED | Modifier.PUBLIC;
3531             }
3532             if (Modifier.isProtected(mods) && refKind == REF_newInvokeSpecial) {
3533                 // cannot "new" a protected ctor in a different package
3534                 mods ^= Modifier.PROTECTED;
3535             }
3536             if (Modifier.isFinal(mods) &&
3537                     MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsSetter(refKind))
3538                 throw m.makeAccessException("unexpected set of a final field", this);
3539             int requestedModes = fixmods(mods);  // adjust 0 => PACKAGE
3540             if ((requestedModes & allowedModes) != 0) {
3541                 if (VerifyAccess.isMemberAccessible(refc, m.getDeclaringClass(),
3542                                                     mods, lookupClass(), previousLookupClass(), allowedModes))
3543                     return;
3544             } else {
3545                 // Protected members can also be checked as if they were package-private.
3546                 if ((requestedModes & PROTECTED) != 0 && (allowedModes & PACKAGE) != 0
3547                         && VerifyAccess.isSamePackage(m.getDeclaringClass(), lookupClass()))
3548                     return;
3549             }
3550             throw m.makeAccessException(accessFailedMessage(refc, m), this);
3551         }
3552 
3553         String accessFailedMessage(Class<?> refc, MemberName m) {
3554             Class<?> defc = m.getDeclaringClass();
3555             int mods = m.getModifiers();
3556             // check the class first:
3557             boolean classOK = (Modifier.isPublic(defc.getModifiers()) &&
3558                                (defc == refc ||
3559                                 Modifier.isPublic(refc.getModifiers())));
3560             if (!classOK && (allowedModes & PACKAGE) != 0) {
3561                 // ignore previous lookup class to check if default package access
3562                 classOK = (VerifyAccess.isClassAccessible(defc, lookupClass(), null, FULL_POWER_MODES) &&
3563                            (defc == refc ||
3564                             VerifyAccess.isClassAccessible(refc, lookupClass(), null, FULL_POWER_MODES)));
3565             }
3566             if (!classOK)
3567                 return "class is not public";
3568             if (Modifier.isPublic(mods))
3569                 return "access to public member failed";  // (how?, module not readable?)
3570             if (Modifier.isPrivate(mods))
3571                 return "member is private";
3572             if (Modifier.isProtected(mods))
3573                 return "member is protected";
3574             return "member is private to package";
3575         }
3576 
3577         private void checkSpecialCaller(Class<?> specialCaller, Class<?> refc) throws IllegalAccessException {
3578             int allowedModes = this.allowedModes;
3579             if (allowedModes == TRUSTED)  return;
3580             if ((lookupModes() & PRIVATE) == 0
3581                 || (specialCaller != lookupClass()
3582                        // ensure non-abstract methods in superinterfaces can be special-invoked
3583                     && !(refc != null && refc.isInterface() && refc.isAssignableFrom(specialCaller))))
3584                 throw new MemberName(specialCaller).
3585                     makeAccessException("no private access for invokespecial", this);
3586         }
3587 
3588         private boolean restrictProtectedReceiver(MemberName method) {
3589             // The accessing class only has the right to use a protected member
3590             // on itself or a subclass.  Enforce that restriction, from JVMS 5.4.4, etc.
3591             if (!method.isProtected() || method.isStatic()
3592                 || allowedModes == TRUSTED
3593                 || method.getDeclaringClass() == lookupClass()
3594                 || VerifyAccess.isSamePackage(method.getDeclaringClass(), lookupClass()))
3595                 return false;
3596             return true;
3597         }
3598         private MethodHandle restrictReceiver(MemberName method, DirectMethodHandle mh, Class<?> caller) throws IllegalAccessException {
3599             assert(!method.isStatic());
3600             // receiver type of mh is too wide; narrow to caller
3601             if (!method.getDeclaringClass().isAssignableFrom(caller)) {
3602                 throw method.makeAccessException("caller class must be a subclass below the method", caller);
3603             }
3604             MethodType rawType = mh.type();
3605             if (caller.isAssignableFrom(rawType.parameterType(0))) return mh; // no need to restrict; already narrow
3606             MethodType narrowType = rawType.changeParameterType(0, caller);
3607             assert(!mh.isVarargsCollector());  // viewAsType will lose varargs-ness
3608             assert(mh.viewAsTypeChecks(narrowType, true));
3609             return mh.copyWith(narrowType, mh.form);
3610         }
3611 
3612         /** Check access and get the requested method. */
3613         private MethodHandle getDirectMethod(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName method, Lookup callerLookup) throws IllegalAccessException {
3614             final boolean doRestrict    = true;
3615             final boolean checkSecurity = true;
3616             return getDirectMethodCommon(refKind, refc, method, checkSecurity, doRestrict, callerLookup);
3617         }
3618         /** Check access and get the requested method, for invokespecial with no restriction on the application of narrowing rules. */
3619         private MethodHandle getDirectMethodNoRestrictInvokeSpecial(Class<?> refc, MemberName method, Lookup callerLookup) throws IllegalAccessException {
3620             final boolean doRestrict    = false;
3621             final boolean checkSecurity = true;
3622             return getDirectMethodCommon(REF_invokeSpecial, refc, method, checkSecurity, doRestrict, callerLookup);
3623         }
3624         /** Check access and get the requested method, eliding security manager checks. */
3625         private MethodHandle getDirectMethodNoSecurityManager(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName method, Lookup callerLookup) throws IllegalAccessException {
3626             final boolean doRestrict    = true;
3627             final boolean checkSecurity = false;  // not needed for reflection or for linking CONSTANT_MH constants
3628             return getDirectMethodCommon(refKind, refc, method, checkSecurity, doRestrict, callerLookup);
3629         }
3630         /** Common code for all methods; do not call directly except from immediately above. */
3631         private MethodHandle getDirectMethodCommon(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName method,
3632                                                    boolean checkSecurity,
3633                                                    boolean doRestrict,
3634                                                    Lookup boundCaller) throws IllegalAccessException {
3635             checkMethod(refKind, refc, method);
3636             // Optionally check with the security manager; this isn't needed for unreflect* calls.
3637             if (checkSecurity)
3638                 checkSecurityManager(refc, method);
3639             assert(!method.isMethodHandleInvoke());
3640 
3641             if (refKind == REF_invokeSpecial &&
3642                 refc != lookupClass() &&
3643                 !refc.isInterface() &&
3644                 refc != lookupClass().getSuperclass() &&
3645                 refc.isAssignableFrom(lookupClass())) {
3646                 assert(!method.getName().equals("<init>"));  // not this code path
3647 
3648                 // Per JVMS 6.5, desc. of invokespecial instruction:
3649                 // If the method is in a superclass of the LC,
3650                 // and if our original search was above LC.super,
3651                 // repeat the search (symbolic lookup) from LC.super
3652                 // and continue with the direct superclass of that class,
3653                 // and so forth, until a match is found or no further superclasses exist.
3654                 // FIXME: MemberName.resolve should handle this instead.
3655                 Class<?> refcAsSuper = lookupClass();
3656                 MemberName m2;
3657                 do {
3658                     refcAsSuper = refcAsSuper.getSuperclass();
3659                     m2 = new MemberName(refcAsSuper,
3660                                         method.getName(),
3661                                         method.getMethodType(),
3662                                         REF_invokeSpecial);
3663                     m2 = IMPL_NAMES.resolveOrNull(refKind, m2, lookupClassOrNull());
3664                 } while (m2 == null &&         // no method is found yet
3665                          refc != refcAsSuper); // search up to refc
3666                 if (m2 == null)  throw new InternalError(method.toString());
3667                 method = m2;
3668                 refc = refcAsSuper;
3669                 // redo basic checks
3670                 checkMethod(refKind, refc, method);
3671             }
3672             DirectMethodHandle dmh = DirectMethodHandle.make(refKind, refc, method, lookupClass());
3673             MethodHandle mh = dmh;
3674             // Optionally narrow the receiver argument to lookupClass using restrictReceiver.
3675             if ((doRestrict && refKind == REF_invokeSpecial) ||
3676                     (MethodHandleNatives.refKindHasReceiver(refKind) && restrictProtectedReceiver(method))) {
3677                 mh = restrictReceiver(method, dmh, lookupClass());
3678             }
3679             mh = maybeBindCaller(method, mh, boundCaller);
3680             mh = mh.setVarargs(method);
3681             return mh;
3682         }
3683         private MethodHandle maybeBindCaller(MemberName method, MethodHandle mh, Lookup boundCaller)
3684                                              throws IllegalAccessException {
3685             if (boundCaller.allowedModes == TRUSTED || !MethodHandleNatives.isCallerSensitive(method))
3686                 return mh;
3687 
3688             // boundCaller must have full privilege access.
3689             // It should have been checked by findBoundCallerLookup. Safe to check this again.
3690             if (!boundCaller.hasFullPrivilegeAccess())
3691                 throw new IllegalAccessException("Attempt to lookup caller-sensitive method using restricted lookup object");
3692 
3693             MethodHandle cbmh = MethodHandleImpl.bindCaller(mh, boundCaller.lookupClass);
3694             // Note: caller will apply varargs after this step happens.
3695             return cbmh;
3696         }
3697 
3698         /** Check access and get the requested field. */
3699         private MethodHandle getDirectField(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName field) throws IllegalAccessException {
3700             final boolean checkSecurity = true;
3701             return getDirectFieldCommon(refKind, refc, field, checkSecurity);
3702         }
3703         /** Check access and get the requested field, eliding security manager checks. */
3704         private MethodHandle getDirectFieldNoSecurityManager(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName field) throws IllegalAccessException {
3705             final boolean checkSecurity = false;  // not needed for reflection or for linking CONSTANT_MH constants
3706             return getDirectFieldCommon(refKind, refc, field, checkSecurity);
3707         }
3708         /** Common code for all fields; do not call directly except from immediately above. */
3709         private MethodHandle getDirectFieldCommon(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName field,
3710                                                   boolean checkSecurity) throws IllegalAccessException {
3711             checkField(refKind, refc, field);
3712             // Optionally check with the security manager; this isn't needed for unreflect* calls.
3713             if (checkSecurity)
3714                 checkSecurityManager(refc, field);
3715             DirectMethodHandle dmh = DirectMethodHandle.make(refc, field);
3716             boolean doRestrict = (MethodHandleNatives.refKindHasReceiver(refKind) &&
3717                                     restrictProtectedReceiver(field));
3718             if (doRestrict)
3719                 return restrictReceiver(field, dmh, lookupClass());
3720             return dmh;
3721         }
3722         private VarHandle getFieldVarHandle(byte getRefKind, byte putRefKind,
3723                                             Class<?> refc, MemberName getField, MemberName putField)
3724                 throws IllegalAccessException {
3725             final boolean checkSecurity = true;
3726             return getFieldVarHandleCommon(getRefKind, putRefKind, refc, getField, putField, checkSecurity);
3727         }
3728         private VarHandle getFieldVarHandleNoSecurityManager(byte getRefKind, byte putRefKind,
3729                                                              Class<?> refc, MemberName getField, MemberName putField)
3730                 throws IllegalAccessException {
3731             final boolean checkSecurity = false;
3732             return getFieldVarHandleCommon(getRefKind, putRefKind, refc, getField, putField, checkSecurity);
3733         }
3734         private VarHandle getFieldVarHandleCommon(byte getRefKind, byte putRefKind,
3735                                                   Class<?> refc, MemberName getField, MemberName putField,
3736                                                   boolean checkSecurity) throws IllegalAccessException {
3737             assert getField.isStatic() == putField.isStatic();
3738             assert getField.isGetter() && putField.isSetter();
3739             assert MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsStatic(getRefKind) == MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsStatic(putRefKind);
3740             assert MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsGetter(getRefKind) && MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsSetter(putRefKind);
3741 
3742             checkField(getRefKind, refc, getField);
3743             if (checkSecurity)
3744                 checkSecurityManager(refc, getField);
3745 
3746             if (!putField.isFinal()) {
3747                 // A VarHandle does not support updates to final fields, any
3748                 // such VarHandle to a final field will be read-only and
3749                 // therefore the following write-based accessibility checks are
3750                 // only required for non-final fields
3751                 checkField(putRefKind, refc, putField);
3752                 if (checkSecurity)
3753                     checkSecurityManager(refc, putField);
3754             }
3755 
3756             boolean doRestrict = (MethodHandleNatives.refKindHasReceiver(getRefKind) &&
3757                                   restrictProtectedReceiver(getField));
3758             if (doRestrict) {
3759                 assert !getField.isStatic();
3760                 // receiver type of VarHandle is too wide; narrow to caller
3761                 if (!getField.getDeclaringClass().isAssignableFrom(lookupClass())) {
3762                     throw getField.makeAccessException("caller class must be a subclass below the method", lookupClass());
3763                 }
3764                 refc = lookupClass();
3765             }
3766             return VarHandles.makeFieldHandle(getField, refc, getField.getFieldType(),
3767                                              this.allowedModes == TRUSTED && !getField.getDeclaringClass().isHidden());
3768         }
3769         /** Check access and get the requested constructor. */
3770         private MethodHandle getDirectConstructor(Class<?> refc, MemberName ctor) throws IllegalAccessException {
3771             final boolean checkSecurity = true;
3772             return getDirectConstructorCommon(refc, ctor, checkSecurity);
3773         }
3774         /** Check access and get the requested constructor, eliding security manager checks. */
3775         private MethodHandle getDirectConstructorNoSecurityManager(Class<?> refc, MemberName ctor) throws IllegalAccessException {
3776             final boolean checkSecurity = false;  // not needed for reflection or for linking CONSTANT_MH constants
3777             return getDirectConstructorCommon(refc, ctor, checkSecurity);
3778         }
3779         /** Common code for all constructors; do not call directly except from immediately above. */
3780         private MethodHandle getDirectConstructorCommon(Class<?> refc, MemberName ctor,
3781                                                   boolean checkSecurity) throws IllegalAccessException {
3782             assert(ctor.isObjectConstructor());
3783             checkAccess(REF_newInvokeSpecial, refc, ctor);
3784             // Optionally check with the security manager; this isn't needed for unreflect* calls.
3785             if (checkSecurity)
3786                 checkSecurityManager(refc, ctor);
3787             assert(!MethodHandleNatives.isCallerSensitive(ctor));  // maybeBindCaller not relevant here
3788             return DirectMethodHandle.make(ctor).setVarargs(ctor);
3789         }
3790 
3791         /** Hook called from the JVM (via MethodHandleNatives) to link MH constants:
3792          */
3793         /*non-public*/
3794         MethodHandle linkMethodHandleConstant(byte refKind, Class<?> defc, String name, Object type)
3795                 throws ReflectiveOperationException {
3796             if (!(type instanceof Class || type instanceof MethodType))
3797                 throw new InternalError("unresolved MemberName");
3798             MemberName member = new MemberName(refKind, defc, name, type);
3799             MethodHandle mh = LOOKASIDE_TABLE.get(member);
3800             if (mh != null) {
3801                 checkSymbolicClass(defc);
3802                 return mh;
3803             }
3804             if (defc == MethodHandle.class && refKind == REF_invokeVirtual) {
3805                 // Treat MethodHandle.invoke and invokeExact specially.
3806                 mh = findVirtualForMH(member.getName(), member.getMethodType());
3807                 if (mh != null) {
3808                     return mh;
3809                 }
3810             } else if (defc == VarHandle.class && refKind == REF_invokeVirtual) {
3811                 // Treat signature-polymorphic methods on VarHandle specially.
3812                 mh = findVirtualForVH(member.getName(), member.getMethodType());
3813                 if (mh != null) {
3814                     return mh;
3815                 }
3816             }
3817             MemberName resolved = resolveOrFail(refKind, member);
3818             mh = getDirectMethodForConstant(refKind, defc, resolved);
3819             if (mh instanceof DirectMethodHandle
3820                     && canBeCached(refKind, defc, resolved)) {
3821                 MemberName key = mh.internalMemberName();
3822                 if (key != null) {
3823                     key = key.asNormalOriginal();
3824                 }
3825                 if (member.equals(key)) {  // better safe than sorry
3826                     LOOKASIDE_TABLE.put(key, (DirectMethodHandle) mh);
3827                 }
3828             }
3829             return mh;
3830         }
3831         private boolean canBeCached(byte refKind, Class<?> defc, MemberName member) {
3832             if (refKind == REF_invokeSpecial) {
3833                 return false;
3834             }
3835             if (!Modifier.isPublic(defc.getModifiers()) ||
3836                     !Modifier.isPublic(member.getDeclaringClass().getModifiers()) ||
3837                     !member.isPublic() ||
3838                     member.isCallerSensitive()) {
3839                 return false;
3840             }
3841             ClassLoader loader = defc.getClassLoader();
3842             if (loader != null) {
3843                 ClassLoader sysl = ClassLoader.getSystemClassLoader();
3844                 boolean found = false;
3845                 while (sysl != null) {
3846                     if (loader == sysl) { found = true; break; }
3847                     sysl = sysl.getParent();
3848                 }
3849                 if (!found) {
3850                     return false;
3851                 }
3852             }
3853             try {
3854                 MemberName resolved2 = publicLookup().resolveOrNull(refKind,
3855                     new MemberName(refKind, defc, member.getName(), member.getType()));
3856                 if (resolved2 == null) {
3857                     return false;
3858                 }
3859                 checkSecurityManager(defc, resolved2);
3860             } catch (SecurityException ex) {
3861                 return false;
3862             }
3863             return true;
3864         }
3865         private MethodHandle getDirectMethodForConstant(byte refKind, Class<?> defc, MemberName member)
3866                 throws ReflectiveOperationException {
3867             if (MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsField(refKind)) {
3868                 return getDirectFieldNoSecurityManager(refKind, defc, member);
3869             } else if (MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsMethod(refKind)) {
3870                 return getDirectMethodNoSecurityManager(refKind, defc, member, findBoundCallerLookup(member));
3871             } else if (refKind == REF_newInvokeSpecial) {
3872                 return getDirectConstructorNoSecurityManager(defc, member);
3873             }
3874             // oops
3875             throw newIllegalArgumentException("bad MethodHandle constant #"+member);
3876         }
3877 
3878         static ConcurrentHashMap<MemberName, DirectMethodHandle> LOOKASIDE_TABLE = new ConcurrentHashMap<>();
3879     }
3880 
3881     /**
3882      * Produces a method handle constructing arrays of a desired type,
3883      * as if by the {@code anewarray} bytecode.
3884      * The return type of the method handle will be the array type.
3885      * The type of its sole argument will be {@code int}, which specifies the size of the array.
3886      *
3887      * <p> If the returned method handle is invoked with a negative
3888      * array size, a {@code NegativeArraySizeException} will be thrown.
3889      *
3890      * @param arrayClass an array type
3891      * @return a method handle which can create arrays of the given type
3892      * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is {@code null}
3893      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code arrayClass} is not an array type
3894      * @see java.lang.reflect.Array#newInstance(Class, int)
3895      * @jvms 6.5 {@code anewarray} Instruction
3896      * @since 9
3897      */
3898     public static MethodHandle arrayConstructor(Class<?> arrayClass) throws IllegalArgumentException {
3899         if (!arrayClass.isArray()) {
3900             throw newIllegalArgumentException("not an array class: " + arrayClass.getName());
3901         }
3902         MethodHandle ani = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_Array_newInstance).
3903                 bindTo(arrayClass.getComponentType());
3904         return ani.asType(ani.type().changeReturnType(arrayClass));
3905     }
3906 
3907     /**
3908      * Produces a method handle returning the length of an array,
3909      * as if by the {@code arraylength} bytecode.
3910      * The type of the method handle will have {@code int} as return type,
3911      * and its sole argument will be the array type.
3912      *
3913      * <p> If the returned method handle is invoked with a {@code null}
3914      * array reference, a {@code NullPointerException} will be thrown.
3915      *
3916      * @param arrayClass an array type
3917      * @return a method handle which can retrieve the length of an array of the given array type
3918      * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is {@code null}
3919      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if arrayClass is not an array type
3920      * @jvms 6.5 {@code arraylength} Instruction
3921      * @since 9
3922      */
3923     public static MethodHandle arrayLength(Class<?> arrayClass) throws IllegalArgumentException {
3924         return MethodHandleImpl.makeArrayElementAccessor(arrayClass, MethodHandleImpl.ArrayAccess.LENGTH);
3925     }

3927     /**
3928      * Produces a method handle giving read access to elements of an array,
3929      * as if by the {@code aaload} bytecode.
3930      * The type of the method handle will have a return type of the array's
3931      * element type.  Its first argument will be the array type,
3932      * and the second will be {@code int}.
3933      *
3934      * <p> When the returned method handle is invoked,
3935      * the array reference and array index are checked.
3936      * A {@code NullPointerException} will be thrown if the array reference
3937      * is {@code null} and an {@code ArrayIndexOutOfBoundsException} will be
3938      * thrown if the index is negative or if it is greater than or equal to
3939      * the length of the array.
3940      *
3941      * @param arrayClass an array type
3942      * @return a method handle which can load values from the given array type
3943      * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
3944      * @throws  IllegalArgumentException if arrayClass is not an array type
3945      * @jvms 6.5 {@code aaload} Instruction
3946      */
3947     public static MethodHandle arrayElementGetter(Class<?> arrayClass) throws IllegalArgumentException {
3948         return MethodHandleImpl.makeArrayElementAccessor(arrayClass, MethodHandleImpl.ArrayAccess.GET);
3949     }
3950 
3951     /**
3952      * Produces a method handle giving write access to elements of an array,
3953      * as if by the {@code astore} bytecode.
3954      * The type of the method handle will have a void return type.
3955      * Its last argument will be the array's element type.
3956      * The first and second arguments will be the array type and int.
3957      *
3958      * <p> When the returned method handle is invoked,
3959      * the array reference and array index are checked.
3960      * A {@code NullPointerException} will be thrown if the array reference
3961      * is {@code null} and an {@code ArrayIndexOutOfBoundsException} will be
3962      * thrown if the index is negative or if it is greater than or equal to
3963      * the length of the array.
3964      *
3965      * @param arrayClass the class of an array
3966      * @return a method handle which can store values into the array type
3967      * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
3968      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if arrayClass is not an array type
3969      * @jvms 6.5 {@code aastore} Instruction
3970      */
3971     public static MethodHandle arrayElementSetter(Class<?> arrayClass) throws IllegalArgumentException {
3972         if (arrayClass.isInlineClass()) {
3973             throw new UnsupportedOperationException();
3974         }
3975         return MethodHandleImpl.makeArrayElementAccessor(arrayClass, MethodHandleImpl.ArrayAccess.SET);
3976     }
3977 
3978     /**
3979      * Produces a VarHandle giving access to elements of an array of type
3980      * {@code arrayClass}.  The VarHandle's variable type is the component type
3981      * of {@code arrayClass} and the list of coordinate types is
3982      * {@code (arrayClass, int)}, where the {@code int} coordinate type
3983      * corresponds to an argument that is an index into an array.
3984      * <p>
3985      * Certain access modes of the returned VarHandle are unsupported under
3986      * the following conditions:
3987      * <ul>
3988      * <li>if the component type is anything other than {@code byte},
3989      *     {@code short}, {@code char}, {@code int}, {@code long},
3990      *     {@code float}, or {@code double} then numeric atomic update access
3991      *     modes are unsupported.
3992      * <li>if the field type is anything other than {@code boolean},
3993      *     {@code byte}, {@code short}, {@code char}, {@code int} or
3994      *     {@code long} then bitwise atomic update access modes are
3995      *     unsupported.
3996      * </ul>
3997      * <p>
3998      * If the component type is {@code float} or {@code double} then numeric
3999      * and atomic update access modes compare values using their bitwise
4000      * representation (see {@link Float#floatToRawIntBits} and
4001      * {@link Double#doubleToRawLongBits}, respectively).
4002      *
4003      * <p> When the returned {@code VarHandle} is invoked,
4004      * the array reference and array index are checked.
4005      * A {@code NullPointerException} will be thrown if the array reference
4006      * is {@code null} and an {@code ArrayIndexOutOfBoundsException} will be
4007      * thrown if the index is negative or if it is greater than or equal to
4008      * the length of the array.
4009      *
4010      * @apiNote
4011      * Bitwise comparison of {@code float} values or {@code double} values,
4012      * as performed by the numeric and atomic update access modes, differ
4013      * from the primitive {@code ==} operator and the {@link Float#equals}
4014      * and {@link Double#equals} methods, specifically with respect to
4015      * comparing NaN values or comparing {@code -0.0} with {@code +0.0}.
4016      * Care should be taken when performing a compare and set or a compare
4017      * and exchange operation with such values since the operation may
4018      * unexpectedly fail.
4019      * There are many possible NaN values that are considered to be
4020      * {@code NaN} in Java, although no IEEE 754 floating-point operation
4021      * provided by Java can distinguish between them.  Operation failure can
4022      * occur if the expected or witness value is a NaN value and it is
4023      * transformed (perhaps in a platform specific manner) into another NaN
4024      * value, and thus has a different bitwise representation (see
4025      * {@link Float#intBitsToFloat} or {@link Double#longBitsToDouble} for more
4026      * details).
4027      * The values {@code -0.0} and {@code +0.0} have different bitwise
4028      * representations but are considered equal when using the primitive
4029      * {@code ==} operator.  Operation failure can occur if, for example, a
4030      * numeric algorithm computes an expected value to be say {@code -0.0}
4031      * and previously computed the witness value to be say {@code +0.0}.
4032      * @param arrayClass the class of an array, of type {@code T[]}
4033      * @return a VarHandle giving access to elements of an array
4034      * @throws NullPointerException if the arrayClass is null
4035      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if arrayClass is not an array type
4036      * @since 9
4037      */
4038     public static VarHandle arrayElementVarHandle(Class<?> arrayClass) throws IllegalArgumentException {
4039         return VarHandles.makeArrayElementHandle(arrayClass);
4040     }
4041 
4042     /**
4043      * Produces a VarHandle giving access to elements of a {@code byte[]} array
4044      * viewed as if it were a different primitive array type, such as
4045      * {@code int[]} or {@code long[]}.
4046      * The VarHandle's variable type is the component type of
4047      * {@code viewArrayClass} and the list of coordinate types is
4048      * {@code (byte[], int)}, where the {@code int} coordinate type
4049      * corresponds to an argument that is an index into a {@code byte[]} array.
4050      * The returned VarHandle accesses bytes at an index in a {@code byte[]}
4051      * array, composing bytes to or from a value of the component type of
4052      * {@code viewArrayClass} according to the given endianness.
4053      * <p>
4054      * The supported component types (variables types) are {@code short},
4055      * {@code char}, {@code int}, {@code long}, {@code float} and
4056      * {@code double}.
4057      * <p>
4058      * Access of bytes at a given index will result in an
4059      * {@code IndexOutOfBoundsException} if the index is less than {@code 0}
4060      * or greater than the {@code byte[]} array length minus the size (in bytes)
4061      * of {@code T}.
4062      * <p>
4063      * Access of bytes at an index may be aligned or misaligned for {@code T},
4064      * with respect to the underlying memory address, {@code A} say, associated
4065      * with the array and index.
4066      * If access is misaligned then access for anything other than the
4067      * {@code get} and {@code set} access modes will result in an
4068      * {@code IllegalStateException}.  In such cases atomic access is only
4069      * guaranteed with respect to the largest power of two that divides the GCD
4070      * of {@code A} and the size (in bytes) of {@code T}.
4071      * If access is aligned then following access modes are supported and are
4072      * guaranteed to support atomic access:
4073      * <ul>
4074      * <li>read write access modes for all {@code T}, with the exception of
4075      *     access modes {@code get} and {@code set} for {@code long} and
4076      *     {@code double} on 32-bit platforms.
4077      * <li>atomic update access modes for {@code int}, {@code long},
4078      *     {@code float} or {@code double}.
4079      *     (Future major platform releases of the JDK may support additional
4080      *     types for certain currently unsupported access modes.)
4081      * <li>numeric atomic update access modes for {@code int} and {@code long}.
4082      *     (Future major platform releases of the JDK may support additional
4083      *     numeric types for certain currently unsupported access modes.)
4084      * <li>bitwise atomic update access modes for {@code int} and {@code long}.
4085      *     (Future major platform releases of the JDK may support additional
4086      *     numeric types for certain currently unsupported access modes.)
4087      * </ul>
4088      * <p>
4089      * Misaligned access, and therefore atomicity guarantees, may be determined
4090      * for {@code byte[]} arrays without operating on a specific array.  Given
4091      * an {@code index}, {@code T} and it's corresponding boxed type,
4092      * {@code T_BOX}, misalignment may be determined as follows:
4093      * <pre>{@code
4094      * int sizeOfT = T_BOX.BYTES;  // size in bytes of T
4095      * int misalignedAtZeroIndex = ByteBuffer.wrap(new byte[0]).
4096      *     alignmentOffset(0, sizeOfT);
4097      * int misalignedAtIndex = (misalignedAtZeroIndex + index) % sizeOfT;
4098      * boolean isMisaligned = misalignedAtIndex != 0;
4099      * }</pre>
4100      * <p>
4101      * If the variable type is {@code float} or {@code double} then atomic
4102      * update access modes compare values using their bitwise representation
4103      * (see {@link Float#floatToRawIntBits} and
4104      * {@link Double#doubleToRawLongBits}, respectively).
4105      * @param viewArrayClass the view array class, with a component type of
4106      * type {@code T}
4107      * @param byteOrder the endianness of the view array elements, as
4108      * stored in the underlying {@code byte} array
4109      * @return a VarHandle giving access to elements of a {@code byte[]} array
4110      * viewed as if elements corresponding to the components type of the view
4111      * array class
4112      * @throws NullPointerException if viewArrayClass or byteOrder is null
4113      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if viewArrayClass is not an array type
4114      * @throws UnsupportedOperationException if the component type of
4115      * viewArrayClass is not supported as a variable type
4116      * @since 9
4117      */
4118     public static VarHandle byteArrayViewVarHandle(Class<?> viewArrayClass,
4119                                      ByteOrder byteOrder) throws IllegalArgumentException {
4120         Objects.requireNonNull(byteOrder);
4121         return VarHandles.byteArrayViewHandle(viewArrayClass,
4122                                               byteOrder == ByteOrder.BIG_ENDIAN);
4123     }
4124 
4125     /**
4126      * Produces a VarHandle giving access to elements of a {@code ByteBuffer}
4127      * viewed as if it were an array of elements of a different primitive
4128      * component type to that of {@code byte}, such as {@code int[]} or
4129      * {@code long[]}.
4130      * The VarHandle's variable type is the component type of
4131      * {@code viewArrayClass} and the list of coordinate types is
4132      * {@code (ByteBuffer, int)}, where the {@code int} coordinate type
4133      * corresponds to an argument that is an index into a {@code byte[]} array.
4134      * The returned VarHandle accesses bytes at an index in a
4135      * {@code ByteBuffer}, composing bytes to or from a value of the component
4136      * type of {@code viewArrayClass} according to the given endianness.
4137      * <p>
4138      * The supported component types (variables types) are {@code short},
4139      * {@code char}, {@code int}, {@code long}, {@code float} and
4140      * {@code double}.
4141      * <p>
4142      * Access will result in a {@code ReadOnlyBufferException} for anything
4143      * other than the read access modes if the {@code ByteBuffer} is read-only.
4144      * <p>
4145      * Access of bytes at a given index will result in an
4146      * {@code IndexOutOfBoundsException} if the index is less than {@code 0}
4147      * or greater than the {@code ByteBuffer} limit minus the size (in bytes) of
4148      * {@code T}.
4149      * <p>
4150      * Access of bytes at an index may be aligned or misaligned for {@code T},
4151      * with respect to the underlying memory address, {@code A} say, associated
4152      * with the {@code ByteBuffer} and index.
4153      * If access is misaligned then access for anything other than the
4154      * {@code get} and {@code set} access modes will result in an
4155      * {@code IllegalStateException}.  In such cases atomic access is only
4156      * guaranteed with respect to the largest power of two that divides the GCD
4157      * of {@code A} and the size (in bytes) of {@code T}.
4158      * If access is aligned then following access modes are supported and are
4159      * guaranteed to support atomic access:
4160      * <ul>
4161      * <li>read write access modes for all {@code T}, with the exception of
4162      *     access modes {@code get} and {@code set} for {@code long} and
4163      *     {@code double} on 32-bit platforms.
4164      * <li>atomic update access modes for {@code int}, {@code long},
4165      *     {@code float} or {@code double}.
4166      *     (Future major platform releases of the JDK may support additional
4167      *     types for certain currently unsupported access modes.)
4168      * <li>numeric atomic update access modes for {@code int} and {@code long}.
4169      *     (Future major platform releases of the JDK may support additional
4170      *     numeric types for certain currently unsupported access modes.)
4171      * <li>bitwise atomic update access modes for {@code int} and {@code long}.
4172      *     (Future major platform releases of the JDK may support additional
4173      *     numeric types for certain currently unsupported access modes.)
4174      * </ul>
4175      * <p>
4176      * Misaligned access, and therefore atomicity guarantees, may be determined
4177      * for a {@code ByteBuffer}, {@code bb} (direct or otherwise), an
4178      * {@code index}, {@code T} and it's corresponding boxed type,
4179      * {@code T_BOX}, as follows:
4180      * <pre>{@code
4181      * int sizeOfT = T_BOX.BYTES;  // size in bytes of T
4182      * ByteBuffer bb = ...
4183      * int misalignedAtIndex = bb.alignmentOffset(index, sizeOfT);
4184      * boolean isMisaligned = misalignedAtIndex != 0;
4185      * }</pre>
4186      * <p>
4187      * If the variable type is {@code float} or {@code double} then atomic
4188      * update access modes compare values using their bitwise representation
4189      * (see {@link Float#floatToRawIntBits} and
4190      * {@link Double#doubleToRawLongBits}, respectively).
4191      * @param viewArrayClass the view array class, with a component type of
4192      * type {@code T}
4193      * @param byteOrder the endianness of the view array elements, as
4194      * stored in the underlying {@code ByteBuffer} (Note this overrides the
4195      * endianness of a {@code ByteBuffer})
4196      * @return a VarHandle giving access to elements of a {@code ByteBuffer}
4197      * viewed as if elements corresponding to the components type of the view
4198      * array class
4199      * @throws NullPointerException if viewArrayClass or byteOrder is null
4200      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if viewArrayClass is not an array type
4201      * @throws UnsupportedOperationException if the component type of
4202      * viewArrayClass is not supported as a variable type
4203      * @since 9
4204      */
4205     public static VarHandle byteBufferViewVarHandle(Class<?> viewArrayClass,
4206                                       ByteOrder byteOrder) throws IllegalArgumentException {
4207         Objects.requireNonNull(byteOrder);
4208         return VarHandles.makeByteBufferViewHandle(viewArrayClass,
4209                                                    byteOrder == ByteOrder.BIG_ENDIAN);
4210     }

4212 
4213     /// method handle invocation (reflective style)
4214 
4215     /**
4216      * Produces a method handle which will invoke any method handle of the
4217      * given {@code type}, with a given number of trailing arguments replaced by
4218      * a single trailing {@code Object[]} array.
4219      * The resulting invoker will be a method handle with the following
4220      * arguments:
4221      * <ul>
4222      * <li>a single {@code MethodHandle} target
4223      * <li>zero or more leading values (counted by {@code leadingArgCount})
4224      * <li>an {@code Object[]} array containing trailing arguments
4225      * </ul>
4226      * <p>
4227      * The invoker will invoke its target like a call to {@link MethodHandle#invoke invoke} with
4228      * the indicated {@code type}.
4229      * That is, if the target is exactly of the given {@code type}, it will behave
4230      * like {@code invokeExact}; otherwise it behave as if {@link MethodHandle#asType asType}
4231      * is used to convert the target to the required {@code type}.
4232      * <p>
4233      * The type of the returned invoker will not be the given {@code type}, but rather
4234      * will have all parameters except the first {@code leadingArgCount}
4235      * replaced by a single array of type {@code Object[]}, which will be
4236      * the final parameter.
4237      * <p>
4238      * Before invoking its target, the invoker will spread the final array, apply
4239      * reference casts as necessary, and unbox and widen primitive arguments.
4240      * If, when the invoker is called, the supplied array argument does
4241      * not have the correct number of elements, the invoker will throw
4242      * an {@link IllegalArgumentException} instead of invoking the target.
4243      * <p>
4244      * This method is equivalent to the following code (though it may be more efficient):
4245      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
4246 MethodHandle invoker = MethodHandles.invoker(type);
4247 int spreadArgCount = type.parameterCount() - leadingArgCount;
4248 invoker = invoker.asSpreader(Object[].class, spreadArgCount);
4249 return invoker;
4250      * }</pre></blockquote>
4251      * This method throws no reflective or security exceptions.
4252      * @param type the desired target type
4253      * @param leadingArgCount number of fixed arguments, to be passed unchanged to the target
4254      * @return a method handle suitable for invoking any method handle of the given type
4255      * @throws NullPointerException if {@code type} is null
4256      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code leadingArgCount} is not in
4257      *                  the range from 0 to {@code type.parameterCount()} inclusive,
4258      *                  or if the resulting method handle's type would have
4259      *          <a href="MethodHandle.html#maxarity">too many parameters</a>
4260      */
4261     public static MethodHandle spreadInvoker(MethodType type, int leadingArgCount) {
4262         if (leadingArgCount < 0 || leadingArgCount > type.parameterCount())
4263             throw newIllegalArgumentException("bad argument count", leadingArgCount);
4264         type = type.asSpreaderType(Object[].class, leadingArgCount, type.parameterCount() - leadingArgCount);
4265         return type.invokers().spreadInvoker(leadingArgCount);
4266     }
4267 
4268     /**
4269      * Produces a special <em>invoker method handle</em> which can be used to
4270      * invoke any method handle of the given type, as if by {@link MethodHandle#invokeExact invokeExact}.
4271      * The resulting invoker will have a type which is
4272      * exactly equal to the desired type, except that it will accept
4273      * an additional leading argument of type {@code MethodHandle}.
4274      * <p>
4275      * This method is equivalent to the following code (though it may be more efficient):
4276      * {@code publicLookup().findVirtual(MethodHandle.class, "invokeExact", type)}
4277      *
4278      * <p style="font-size:smaller;">
4279      * <em>Discussion:</em>
4280      * Invoker method handles can be useful when working with variable method handles
4281      * of unknown types.
4282      * For example, to emulate an {@code invokeExact} call to a variable method
4283      * handle {@code M}, extract its type {@code T},
4284      * look up the invoker method {@code X} for {@code T},
4285      * and call the invoker method, as {@code X.invoke(T, A...)}.
4286      * (It would not work to call {@code X.invokeExact}, since the type {@code T}
4287      * is unknown.)
4288      * If spreading, collecting, or other argument transformations are required,
4289      * they can be applied once to the invoker {@code X} and reused on many {@code M}
4290      * method handle values, as long as they are compatible with the type of {@code X}.
4291      * <p style="font-size:smaller;">
4292      * <em>(Note:  The invoker method is not available via the Core Reflection API.
4293      * An attempt to call {@linkplain java.lang.reflect.Method#invoke java.lang.reflect.Method.invoke}
4294      * on the declared {@code invokeExact} or {@code invoke} method will raise an
4295      * {@link java.lang.UnsupportedOperationException UnsupportedOperationException}.)</em>
4296      * <p>
4297      * This method throws no reflective or security exceptions.
4298      * @param type the desired target type
4299      * @return a method handle suitable for invoking any method handle of the given type
4300      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the resulting method handle's type would have
4301      *          <a href="MethodHandle.html#maxarity">too many parameters</a>
4302      */
4303     public static MethodHandle exactInvoker(MethodType type) {
4304         return type.invokers().exactInvoker();
4305     }
4306 
4307     /**
4308      * Produces a special <em>invoker method handle</em> which can be used to
4309      * invoke any method handle compatible with the given type, as if by {@link MethodHandle#invoke invoke}.
4310      * The resulting invoker will have a type which is
4311      * exactly equal to the desired type, except that it will accept
4312      * an additional leading argument of type {@code MethodHandle}.
4313      * <p>
4314      * Before invoking its target, if the target differs from the expected type,
4315      * the invoker will apply reference casts as
4316      * necessary and box, unbox, or widen primitive values, as if by {@link MethodHandle#asType asType}.
4317      * Similarly, the return value will be converted as necessary.
4318      * If the target is a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector variable arity method handle},
4319      * the required arity conversion will be made, again as if by {@link MethodHandle#asType asType}.
4320      * <p>
4321      * This method is equivalent to the following code (though it may be more efficient):
4322      * {@code publicLookup().findVirtual(MethodHandle.class, "invoke", type)}
4323      * <p style="font-size:smaller;">
4324      * <em>Discussion:</em>
4325      * A {@linkplain MethodType#genericMethodType general method type} is one which
4326      * mentions only {@code Object} arguments and return values.
4327      * An invoker for such a type is capable of calling any method handle
4328      * of the same arity as the general type.
4329      * <p style="font-size:smaller;">
4330      * <em>(Note:  The invoker method is not available via the Core Reflection API.
4331      * An attempt to call {@linkplain java.lang.reflect.Method#invoke java.lang.reflect.Method.invoke}
4332      * on the declared {@code invokeExact} or {@code invoke} method will raise an
4333      * {@link java.lang.UnsupportedOperationException UnsupportedOperationException}.)</em>
4334      * <p>
4335      * This method throws no reflective or security exceptions.
4336      * @param type the desired target type
4337      * @return a method handle suitable for invoking any method handle convertible to the given type
4338      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the resulting method handle's type would have
4339      *          <a href="MethodHandle.html#maxarity">too many parameters</a>
4340      */
4341     public static MethodHandle invoker(MethodType type) {
4342         return type.invokers().genericInvoker();
4343     }

4349      * The resulting invoker will have a type which is exactly equal to the

4356      *         any VarHandle whose access mode type is of the given type.

4359     public static MethodHandle varHandleExactInvoker(VarHandle.AccessMode accessMode, MethodType type) {

4366      * associated access mode type is compatible with the given type.
4367      * The resulting invoker will have a type which is exactly equal to the

4395 
4396      /// method handle modification (creation from other method handles)
4397 
4398     /**
4399      * Produces a method handle which adapts the type of the
4400      * given method handle to a new type by pairwise argument and return type conversion.
4401      * The original type and new type must have the same number of arguments.
4402      * The resulting method handle is guaranteed to report a type
4403      * which is equal to the desired new type.
4404      * <p>
4405      * If the original type and new type are equal, returns target.
4406      * <p>
4407      * The same conversions are allowed as for {@link MethodHandle#asType MethodHandle.asType},
4408      * and some additional conversions are also applied if those conversions fail.
4409      * Given types <em>T0</em>, <em>T1</em>, one of the following conversions is applied
4410      * if possible, before or instead of any conversions done by {@code asType}:
4411      * <ul>
4412      * <li>If <em>T0</em> and <em>T1</em> are references, and <em>T1</em> is an interface type,
4413      *     then the value of type <em>T0</em> is passed as a <em>T1</em> without a cast.
4414      *     (This treatment of interfaces follows the usage of the bytecode verifier.)
4415      * <li>If <em>T0</em> is boolean and <em>T1</em> is another primitive,
4416      *     the boolean is converted to a byte value, 1 for true, 0 for false.
4417      *     (This treatment follows the usage of the bytecode verifier.)
4418      * <li>If <em>T1</em> is boolean and <em>T0</em> is another primitive,
4419      *     <em>T0</em> is converted to byte via Java casting conversion (JLS 5.5),
4420      *     and the low order bit of the result is tested, as if by {@code (x & 1) != 0}.
4421      * <li>If <em>T0</em> and <em>T1</em> are primitives other than boolean,
4422      *     then a Java casting conversion (JLS 5.5) is applied.
4423      *     (Specifically, <em>T0</em> will convert to <em>T1</em> by
4424      *     widening and/or narrowing.)
4425      * <li>If <em>T0</em> is a reference and <em>T1</em> a primitive, an unboxing
4426      *     conversion will be applied at runtime, possibly followed
4427      *     by a Java casting conversion (JLS 5.5) on the primitive value,
4428      *     possibly followed by a conversion from byte to boolean by testing
4429      *     the low-order bit.
4430      * <li>If <em>T0</em> is a reference and <em>T1</em> a primitive,
4431      *     and if the reference is null at runtime, a zero value is introduced.
4432      * </ul>
4433      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are retyped
4434      * @param newType the expected type of the new method handle
4435      * @return a method handle which delegates to the target after performing
4436      *           any necessary argument conversions, and arranges for any
4437      *           necessary return value conversions
4438      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
4439      * @throws WrongMethodTypeException if the conversion cannot be made
4440      * @see MethodHandle#asType
4441      */
4442     public static MethodHandle explicitCastArguments(MethodHandle target, MethodType newType) {
4443         explicitCastArgumentsChecks(target, newType);
4444         // use the asTypeCache when possible:
4445         MethodType oldType = target.type();
4446         if (oldType == newType)  return target;
4447         if (oldType.explicitCastEquivalentToAsType(newType)) {
4448             return target.asFixedArity().asType(newType);
4449         }
4450         return MethodHandleImpl.makePairwiseConvert(target, newType, false);
4451     }
4452 
4453     private static void explicitCastArgumentsChecks(MethodHandle target, MethodType newType) {
4454         if (target.type().parameterCount() != newType.parameterCount()) {
4455             throw new WrongMethodTypeException("cannot explicitly cast " + target + " to " + newType);
4456         }
4457     }
4458 
4459     /**
4460      * Produces a method handle which adapts the calling sequence of the
4461      * given method handle to a new type, by reordering the arguments.
4462      * The resulting method handle is guaranteed to report a type
4463      * which is equal to the desired new type.
4464      * <p>
4465      * The given array controls the reordering.
4466      * Call {@code #I} the number of incoming parameters (the value
4467      * {@code newType.parameterCount()}, and call {@code #O} the number
4468      * of outgoing parameters (the value {@code target.type().parameterCount()}).
4469      * Then the length of the reordering array must be {@code #O},
4470      * and each element must be a non-negative number less than {@code #I}.
4471      * For every {@code N} less than {@code #O}, the {@code N}-th
4472      * outgoing argument will be taken from the {@code I}-th incoming
4473      * argument, where {@code I} is {@code reorder[N]}.
4474      * <p>
4475      * No argument or return value conversions are applied.
4476      * The type of each incoming argument, as determined by {@code newType},
4477      * must be identical to the type of the corresponding outgoing parameter
4478      * or parameters in the target method handle.
4479      * The return type of {@code newType} must be identical to the return
4480      * type of the original target.
4481      * <p>
4482      * The reordering array need not specify an actual permutation.
4483      * An incoming argument will be duplicated if its index appears
4484      * more than once in the array, and an incoming argument will be dropped
4485      * if its index does not appear in the array.
4486      * As in the case of {@link #dropArguments(MethodHandle,int,List) dropArguments},
4487      * incoming arguments which are not mentioned in the reordering array
4488      * may be of any type, as determined only by {@code newType}.
4489      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
4490 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
4491 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
4492 ...
4493 MethodType intfn1 = methodType(int.class, int.class);
4494 MethodType intfn2 = methodType(int.class, int.class, int.class);
4495 MethodHandle sub = ... (int x, int y) -> (x-y) ...;
4496 assert(sub.type().equals(intfn2));
4497 MethodHandle sub1 = permuteArguments(sub, intfn2, 0, 1);
4498 MethodHandle rsub = permuteArguments(sub, intfn2, 1, 0);
4499 assert((int)rsub.invokeExact(1, 100) == 99);
4500 MethodHandle add = ... (int x, int y) -> (x+y) ...;
