5911                                 Class<? extends Throwable> exType,
5912                                 MethodHandle handler) {
5913         MethodType ttype = target.type();
5914         MethodType htype = handler.type();
5915         if (!Throwable.class.isAssignableFrom(exType))
5916             throw new ClassCastException(exType.getName());
5917         if (htype.parameterCount() < 1 ||
5918             !htype.parameterType(0).isAssignableFrom(exType))
5919             throw newIllegalArgumentException("handler does not accept exception type "+exType);
5920         if (htype.returnType() != ttype.returnType())
5921             throw misMatchedTypes("target and handler return types", ttype, htype);
5922         handler = dropArgumentsToMatch(handler, 1, ttype.parameterList(), 0, true);
5923         if (handler == null) {
5924             throw misMatchedTypes("target and handler types", ttype, htype);
5925         }
5926         return MethodHandleImpl.makeGuardWithCatch(target, exType, handler);
5927     }
5928 
5929     /**
5930      * Produces a method handle which will throw exceptions of the given {@code exType}.
5931      * The method handle will accept a single argument of {@code exType},
5932      * and immediately throw it as an exception.
5933      * The method type will nominally specify a return of {@code returnType}.
5934      * The return type may be anything convenient:  It doesn't matter to the
5935      * method handle's behavior, since it will never return normally.
5936      * @param returnType the return type of the desired method handle
5937      * @param exType the parameter type of the desired method handle
5938      * @return method handle which can throw the given exceptions
5939      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5940      */
5941     public static MethodHandle throwException(Class<?> returnType, Class<? extends Throwable> exType) {
5942         if (!Throwable.class.isAssignableFrom(exType))
5943             throw new ClassCastException(exType.getName());
5944         return MethodHandleImpl.throwException(methodType(returnType, exType));
5945     }
5946 
5947     /**
5948      * Constructs a method handle representing a loop with several loop variables that are updated and checked upon each
5949      * iteration. Upon termination of the loop due to one of the predicates, a corresponding finalizer is run and
5950      * delivers the loop's result, which is the return value of the resulting handle.
5951      * <p>
5952      * Intuitively, every loop is formed by one or more "clauses", each specifying a local <em>iteration variable</em> and/or a loop
5953      * exit. Each iteration of the loop executes each clause in order. A clause can optionally update its iteration
5954      * variable; it can also optionally perform a test and conditional loop exit. In order to express this logic in
5955      * terms of method handles, each clause will specify up to four independent actions:<ul>
5956      * <li><em>init:</em> Before the loop executes, the initialization of an iteration variable {@code v} of type {@code V}.
5957      * <li><em>step:</em> When a clause executes, an update step for the iteration variable {@code v}.
5958      * <li><em>pred:</em> When a clause executes, a predicate execution to test for loop exit.
5959      * <li><em>fini:</em> If a clause causes a loop exit, a finalizer execution to compute the loop's return value.
5960      * </ul>
5961      * The full sequence of all iteration variable types, in clause order, will be notated as {@code (V...)}.
5962      * The values themselves will be {@code (v...)}.  When we speak of "parameter lists", we will usually
5963      * be referring to types, but in some contexts (describing execution) the lists will be of actual values.
5964      * <p>
5965      * Some of these clause parts may be omitted according to certain rules, and useful default behavior is provided in
5966      * this case. See below for a detailed description.
5967      * <p>
5968      * <em>Parameters optional everywhere:</em>
5969      * Each clause function is allowed but not required to accept a parameter for each iteration variable {@code v}.
5970      * As an exception, the init functions cannot take any {@code v} parameters,
5971      * because those values are not yet computed when the init functions are executed.
5972      * Any clause function may neglect to take any trailing subsequence of parameters it is entitled to take.
5973      * In fact, any clause function may take no arguments at all.
5974      * <p>
5975      * <em>Loop parameters:</em>
5976      * A clause function may take all the iteration variable values it is entitled to, in which case
5977      * it may also take more trailing parameters. Such extra values are called <em>loop parameters</em>,
5978      * with their types and values notated as {@code (A...)} and {@code (a...)}.
5979      * These become the parameters of the resulting loop handle, to be supplied whenever the loop is executed.
5980      * (Since init functions do not accept iteration variables {@code v}, any parameter to an
5981      * init function is automatically a loop parameter {@code a}.)
5982      * As with iteration variables, clause functions are allowed but not required to accept loop parameters.
5983      * These loop parameters act as loop-invariant values visible across the whole loop.
5984      * <p>
5985      * <em>Parameters visible everywhere:</em>
5986      * Each non-init clause function is permitted to observe the entire loop state, because it can be passed the full
5987      * list {@code (v... a...)} of current iteration variable values and incoming loop parameters.
5988      * The init functions can observe initial pre-loop state, in the form {@code (a...)}.
5989      * Most clause functions will not need all of this information, but they will be formally connected to it
5990      * as if by {@link #dropArguments}.
5991      * <a id="astar"></a>
5992      * More specifically, we shall use the notation {@code (V*)} to express an arbitrary prefix of a full
5993      * sequence {@code (V...)} (and likewise for {@code (v*)}, {@code (A*)}, {@code (a*)}).
5994      * In that notation, the general form of an init function parameter list
5995      * is {@code (A*)}, and the general form of a non-init function parameter list is {@code (V*)} or {@code (V... A*)}.
5996      * <p>
5997      * <em>Checking clause structure:</em>
5998      * Given a set of clauses, there is a number of checks and adjustments performed to connect all the parts of the
5999      * loop. They are spelled out in detail in the steps below. In these steps, every occurrence of the word "must"
6000      * corresponds to a place where {@link IllegalArgumentException} will be thrown if the required constraint is not
6001      * met by the inputs to the loop combinator.
6002      * <p>
6003      * <em>Effectively identical sequences:</em>
6004      * <a id="effid"></a>
6005      * A parameter list {@code A} is defined to be <em>effectively identical</em> to another parameter list {@code B}
6006      * if {@code A} and {@code B} are identical, or if {@code A} is shorter and is identical with a proper prefix of {@code B}.
6007      * When speaking of an unordered set of parameter lists, we say they the set is "effectively identical"
6008      * as a whole if the set contains a longest list, and all members of the set are effectively identical to
6009      * that longest list.
6010      * For example, any set of type sequences of the form {@code (V*)} is effectively identical,
6011      * and the same is true if more sequences of the form {@code (V... A*)} are added.
6012      * <p>
6013      * <em>Step 0: Determine clause structure.</em><ol type="a">
6014      * <li>The clause array (of type {@code MethodHandle[][]}) must be non-{@code null} and contain at least one element.
6015      * <li>The clause array may not contain {@code null}s or sub-arrays longer than four elements.
6016      * <li>Clauses shorter than four elements are treated as if they were padded by {@code null} elements to length
6017      * four. Padding takes place by appending elements to the array.
6018      * <li>Clauses with all {@code null}s are disregarded.
6019      * <li>Each clause is treated as a four-tuple of functions, called "init", "step", "pred", and "fini".
6020      * </ol>
6021      * <p>
6022      * <em>Step 1A: Determine iteration variable types {@code (V...)}.</em><ol type="a">
6023      * <li>The iteration variable type for each clause is determined using the clause's init and step return types.
6024      * <li>If both functions are omitted, there is no iteration variable for the corresponding clause ({@code void} is
6025      * used as the type to indicate that). If one of them is omitted, the other's return type defines the clause's
6026      * iteration variable type. If both are given, the common return type (they must be identical) defines the clause's
6027      * iteration variable type.
6028      * <li>Form the list of return types (in clause order), omitting all occurrences of {@code void}.
6029      * <li>This list of types is called the "iteration variable types" ({@code (V...)}).
6030      * </ol>
6031      * <p>
6032      * <em>Step 1B: Determine loop parameters {@code (A...)}.</em><ul>
6033      * <li>Examine and collect init function parameter lists (which are of the form {@code (A*)}).
6034      * <li>Examine and collect the suffixes of the step, pred, and fini parameter lists, after removing the iteration variable types.
6035      * (They must have the form {@code (V... A*)}; collect the {@code (A*)} parts only.)
6036      * <li>Do not collect suffixes from step, pred, and fini parameter lists that do not begin with all the iteration variable types.
6037      * (These types will be checked in step 2, along with all the clause function types.)
6038      * <li>Omitted clause functions are ignored.  (Equivalently, they are deemed to have empty parameter lists.)
6039      * <li>All of the collected parameter lists must be effectively identical.
6040      * <li>The longest parameter list (which is necessarily unique) is called the "external parameter list" ({@code (A...)}).
6041      * <li>If there is no such parameter list, the external parameter list is taken to be the empty sequence.
6042      * <li>The combined list consisting of iteration variable types followed by the external parameter types is called
6043      * the "internal parameter list".
6044      * </ul>
6045      * <p>
6046      * <em>Step 1C: Determine loop return type.</em><ol type="a">
6047      * <li>Examine fini function return types, disregarding omitted fini functions.
6048      * <li>If there are no fini functions, the loop return type is {@code void}.
6049      * <li>Otherwise, the common return type {@code R} of the fini functions (their return types must be identical) defines the loop return
6050      * type.
6051      * </ol>
6052      * <p>
6053      * <em>Step 1D: Check other types.</em><ol type="a">
6054      * <li>There must be at least one non-omitted pred function.
6055      * <li>Every non-omitted pred function must have a {@code boolean} return type.
6056      * </ol>
6057      * <p>
6058      * <em>Step 2: Determine parameter lists.</em><ol type="a">
6059      * <li>The parameter list for the resulting loop handle will be the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6060      * <li>The parameter list for init functions will be adjusted to the external parameter list.
6061      * (Note that their parameter lists are already effectively identical to this list.)
6062      * <li>The parameter list for every non-omitted, non-init (step, pred, and fini) function must be
6063      * effectively identical to the internal parameter list {@code (V... A...)}.
6064      * </ol>
6065      * <p>
6066      * <em>Step 3: Fill in omitted functions.</em><ol type="a">
6067      * <li>If an init function is omitted, use a {@linkplain #empty default value} for the clause's iteration variable
6068      * type.
6069      * <li>If a step function is omitted, use an {@linkplain #identity identity function} of the clause's iteration
6070      * variable type; insert dropped argument parameters before the identity function parameter for the non-{@code void}
6071      * iteration variables of preceding clauses. (This will turn the loop variable into a local loop invariant.)
6072      * <li>If a pred function is omitted, use a constant {@code true} function. (This will keep the loop going, as far
6073      * as this clause is concerned.  Note that in such cases the corresponding fini function is unreachable.)
6074      * <li>If a fini function is omitted, use a {@linkplain #empty default value} for the
6075      * loop return type.
6076      * </ol>
6077      * <p>
6078      * <em>Step 4: Fill in missing parameter types.</em><ol type="a">
6079      * <li>At this point, every init function parameter list is effectively identical to the external parameter list {@code (A...)},
6080      * but some lists may be shorter. For every init function with a short parameter list, pad out the end of the list.
6081      * <li>At this point, every non-init function parameter list is effectively identical to the internal parameter
6082      * list {@code (V... A...)}, but some lists may be shorter. For every non-init function with a short parameter list,
6083      * pad out the end of the list.
6084      * <li>Argument lists are padded out by {@linkplain #dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandle, int, List, int) dropping unused trailing arguments}.
6085      * </ol>
6086      * <p>
6087      * <em>Final observations.</em><ol type="a">
6088      * <li>After these steps, all clauses have been adjusted by supplying omitted functions and arguments.
6089      * <li>All init functions have a common parameter type list {@code (A...)}, which the final loop handle will also have.
6090      * <li>All fini functions have a common return type {@code R}, which the final loop handle will also have.
6091      * <li>All non-init functions have a common parameter type list {@code (V... A...)}, of
6092      * (non-{@code void}) iteration variables {@code V} followed by loop parameters.
6093      * <li>Each pair of init and step functions agrees in their return type {@code V}.
6094      * <li>Each non-init function will be able to observe the current values {@code (v...)} of all iteration variables.
6095      * <li>Every function will be able to observe the incoming values {@code (a...)} of all loop parameters.
6096      * </ol>
6097      * <p>
6098      * <em>Example.</em> As a consequence of step 1A above, the {@code loop} combinator has the following property:
6099      * <ul>
6100      * <li>Given {@code N} clauses {@code Cn = {null, Sn, Pn}} with {@code n = 1..N}.
6101      * <li>Suppose predicate handles {@code Pn} are either {@code null} or have no parameters.
6102      * (Only one {@code Pn} has to be non-{@code null}.)
6103      * <li>Suppose step handles {@code Sn} have signatures {@code (B1..BX)Rn}, for some constant {@code X>=N}.
6104      * <li>Suppose {@code Q} is the count of non-void types {@code Rn}, and {@code (V1...VQ)} is the sequence of those types.
6105      * <li>It must be that {@code Vn == Bn} for {@code n = 1..min(X,Q)}.
6106      * <li>The parameter types {@code Vn} will be interpreted as loop-local state elements {@code (V...)}.
6107      * <li>Any remaining types {@code BQ+1..BX} (if {@code Q<X}) will determine
6108      * the resulting loop handle's parameter types {@code (A...)}.
6109      * </ul>
6110      * In this example, the loop handle parameters {@code (A...)} were derived from the step functions,
6111      * which is natural if most of the loop computation happens in the steps.  For some loops,
6112      * the burden of computation might be heaviest in the pred functions, and so the pred functions
6113      * might need to accept the loop parameter values.  For loops with complex exit logic, the fini
6114      * functions might need to accept loop parameters, and likewise for loops with complex entry logic,
6115      * where the init functions will need the extra parameters.  For such reasons, the rules for
6116      * determining these parameters are as symmetric as possible, across all clause parts.
6117      * In general, the loop parameters function as common invariant values across the whole
6118      * loop, while the iteration variables function as common variant values, or (if there is
6119      * no step function) as internal loop invariant temporaries.
6120      * <p>
6121      * <em>Loop execution.</em><ol type="a">
6122      * <li>When the loop is called, the loop input values are saved in locals, to be passed to
6123      * every clause function. These locals are loop invariant.
6124      * <li>Each init function is executed in clause order (passing the external arguments {@code (a...)})
6125      * and the non-{@code void} values are saved (as the iteration variables {@code (v...)}) into locals.
6126      * These locals will be loop varying (unless their steps behave as identity functions, as noted above).
6127      * <li>All function executions (except init functions) will be passed the internal parameter list, consisting of
6128      * the non-{@code void} iteration values {@code (v...)} (in clause order) and then the loop inputs {@code (a...)}
6129      * (in argument order).
6130      * <li>The step and pred functions are then executed, in clause order (step before pred), until a pred function
6131      * returns {@code false}.
6132      * <li>The non-{@code void} result from a step function call is used to update the corresponding value in the
6133      * sequence {@code (v...)} of loop variables.
6134      * The updated value is immediately visible to all subsequent function calls.
6135      * <li>If a pred function returns {@code false}, the corresponding fini function is called, and the resulting value
6136      * (of type {@code R}) is returned from the loop as a whole.
6137      * <li>If all the pred functions always return true, no fini function is ever invoked, and the loop cannot exit
6138      * except by throwing an exception.
6139      * </ol>
6140      * <p>
6141      * <em>Usage tips.</em>
6142      * <ul>
6143      * <li>Although each step function will receive the current values of <em>all</em> the loop variables,
6144      * sometimes a step function only needs to observe the current value of its own variable.
6145      * In that case, the step function may need to explicitly {@linkplain #dropArguments drop all preceding loop variables}.
6146      * This will require mentioning their types, in an expression like {@code dropArguments(step, 0, V0.class, ...)}.
6147      * <li>Loop variables are not required to vary; they can be loop invariant.  A clause can create
6148      * a loop invariant by a suitable init function with no step, pred, or fini function.  This may be
6149      * useful to "wire" an incoming loop argument into the step or pred function of an adjacent loop variable.
6150      * <li>If some of the clause functions are virtual methods on an instance, the instance
6151      * itself can be conveniently placed in an initial invariant loop "variable", using an initial clause
6152      * like {@code new MethodHandle[]{identity(ObjType.class)}}.  In that case, the instance reference
6153      * will be the first iteration variable value, and it will be easy to use virtual
6154      * methods as clause parts, since all of them will take a leading instance reference matching that value.
6155      * </ul>
6156      * <p>
6157      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. As above, {@code V} and {@code v} represent the types
6158      * and values of loop variables; {@code A} and {@code a} represent arguments passed to the whole loop;
6159      * and {@code R} is the common result type of all finalizers as well as of the resulting loop.
6160      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6161      * V... init...(A...);
6162      * boolean pred...(V..., A...);
6163      * V... step...(V..., A...);
6164      * R fini...(V..., A...);
6165      * R loop(A... a) {
6166      *   V... v... = init...(a...);
6167      *   for (;;) {
6168      *     for ((v, p, s, f) in (v..., pred..., step..., fini...)) {
6169      *       v = s(v..., a...);
6170      *       if (!p(v..., a...)) {
6171      *         return f(v..., a...);
6172      *       }
6173      *     }
6174      *   }
6175      * }
6176      * }</pre></blockquote>
6177      * Note that the parameter type lists {@code (V...)} and {@code (A...)} have been expanded
6178      * to their full length, even though individual clause functions may neglect to take them all.
6179      * As noted above, missing parameters are filled in as if by {@link #dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandle, int, List, int)}.
6180      *
6181      * @apiNote Example:
6182      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6183      * // iterative implementation of the factorial function as a loop handle
6184      * static int one(int k) { return 1; }
6185      * static int inc(int i, int acc, int k) { return i + 1; }
6186      * static int mult(int i, int acc, int k) { return i * acc; }
6187      * static boolean pred(int i, int acc, int k) { return i < k; }
6188      * static int fin(int i, int acc, int k) { return acc; }
6189      * // assume MH_one, MH_inc, MH_mult, MH_pred, and MH_fin are handles to the above methods
6190      * // null initializer for counter, should initialize to 0
6191      * MethodHandle[] counterClause = new MethodHandle[]{null, MH_inc};
6192      * MethodHandle[] accumulatorClause = new MethodHandle[]{MH_one, MH_mult, MH_pred, MH_fin};
6193      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.loop(counterClause, accumulatorClause);
6194      * assertEquals(120, loop.invoke(5));
6195      * }</pre></blockquote>
6196      * The same example, dropping arguments and using combinators:
6197      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6198      * // simplified implementation of the factorial function as a loop handle
6199      * static int inc(int i) { return i + 1; } // drop acc, k
6200      * static int mult(int i, int acc) { return i * acc; } //drop k
6201      * static boolean cmp(int i, int k) { return i < k; }
6202      * // assume MH_inc, MH_mult, and MH_cmp are handles to the above methods
6203      * // null initializer for counter, should initialize to 0
6204      * MethodHandle MH_one = MethodHandles.constant(int.class, 1);
6205      * MethodHandle MH_pred = MethodHandles.dropArguments(MH_cmp, 1, int.class); // drop acc
6206      * MethodHandle MH_fin = MethodHandles.dropArguments(MethodHandles.identity(int.class), 0, int.class); // drop i
6207      * MethodHandle[] counterClause = new MethodHandle[]{null, MH_inc};
6208      * MethodHandle[] accumulatorClause = new MethodHandle[]{MH_one, MH_mult, MH_pred, MH_fin};
6209      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.loop(counterClause, accumulatorClause);
6210      * assertEquals(720, loop.invoke(6));
6211      * }</pre></blockquote>
6212      * A similar example, using a helper object to hold a loop parameter:
6213      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6214      * // instance-based implementation of the factorial function as a loop handle
6215      * static class FacLoop {
6216      *   final int k;
6217      *   FacLoop(int k) { this.k = k; }
6218      *   int inc(int i) { return i + 1; }
6219      *   int mult(int i, int acc) { return i * acc; }
6220      *   boolean pred(int i) { return i < k; }
6221      *   int fin(int i, int acc) { return acc; }
6222      * }
6223      * // assume MH_FacLoop is a handle to the constructor
6224      * // assume MH_inc, MH_mult, MH_pred, and MH_fin are handles to the above methods
6225      * // null initializer for counter, should initialize to 0
6226      * MethodHandle MH_one = MethodHandles.constant(int.class, 1);
6227      * MethodHandle[] instanceClause = new MethodHandle[]{MH_FacLoop};
6228      * MethodHandle[] counterClause = new MethodHandle[]{null, MH_inc};
6229      * MethodHandle[] accumulatorClause = new MethodHandle[]{MH_one, MH_mult, MH_pred, MH_fin};
6230      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.loop(instanceClause, counterClause, accumulatorClause);
6231      * assertEquals(5040, loop.invoke(7));
6232      * }</pre></blockquote>
6233      *
6234      * @param clauses an array of arrays (4-tuples) of {@link MethodHandle}s adhering to the rules described above.
6235      *
6236      * @return a method handle embodying the looping behavior as defined by the arguments.
6237      *
6238      * @throws IllegalArgumentException in case any of the constraints described above is violated.
6239      *
6240      * @see MethodHandles#whileLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6241      * @see MethodHandles#doWhileLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6242      * @see MethodHandles#countedLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6243      * @see MethodHandles#iteratedLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6244      * @since 9
6245      */
6246     public static MethodHandle loop(MethodHandle[]... clauses) {
6247         // Step 0: determine clause structure.
6248         loopChecks0(clauses);
6249 
6250         List<MethodHandle> init = new ArrayList<>();
6251         List<MethodHandle> step = new ArrayList<>();
6252         List<MethodHandle> pred = new ArrayList<>();
6253         List<MethodHandle> fini = new ArrayList<>();
6254 
6255         Stream.of(clauses).filter(c -> Stream.of(c).anyMatch(Objects::nonNull)).forEach(clause -> {
6256             init.add(clause[0]); // all clauses have at least length 1
6257             step.add(clause.length <= 1 ? null : clause[1]);
6258             pred.add(clause.length <= 2 ? null : clause[2]);
6259             fini.add(clause.length <= 3 ? null : clause[3]);
6260         });
6261 
6262         assert Stream.of(init, step, pred, fini).map(List::size).distinct().count() == 1;
6263         final int nclauses = init.size();
6264 
6265         // Step 1A: determine iteration variables (V...).
6266         final List<Class<?>> iterationVariableTypes = new ArrayList<>();
6267         for (int i = 0; i < nclauses; ++i) {
6268             MethodHandle in = init.get(i);
6269             MethodHandle st = step.get(i);
6270             if (in == null && st == null) {
6271                 iterationVariableTypes.add(void.class);
6272             } else if (in != null && st != null) {
6273                 loopChecks1a(i, in, st);
6274                 iterationVariableTypes.add(in.type().returnType());
6275             } else {
6276                 iterationVariableTypes.add(in == null ? st.type().returnType() : in.type().returnType());
6277             }
6278         }
6279         final List<Class<?>> commonPrefix = iterationVariableTypes.stream().filter(t -> t != void.class).
6280                 collect(Collectors.toList());
6281 
6282         // Step 1B: determine loop parameters (A...).
6283         final List<Class<?>> commonSuffix = buildCommonSuffix(init, step, pred, fini, commonPrefix.size());
6284         loopChecks1b(init, commonSuffix);
6285 
6286         // Step 1C: determine loop return type.
6287         // Step 1D: check other types.
6288         // local variable required here; see JDK-8223553
6289         Stream<Class<?>> cstream = fini.stream().filter(Objects::nonNull).map(MethodHandle::type)
6290                 .map(MethodType::returnType);
6291         final Class<?> loopReturnType = cstream.findFirst().orElse(void.class);
6292         loopChecks1cd(pred, fini, loopReturnType);
6293 
6294         // Step 2: determine parameter lists.
6295         final List<Class<?>> commonParameterSequence = new ArrayList<>(commonPrefix);
6296         commonParameterSequence.addAll(commonSuffix);
6297         loopChecks2(step, pred, fini, commonParameterSequence);
6298 
6299         // Step 3: fill in omitted functions.
6300         for (int i = 0; i < nclauses; ++i) {
6301             Class<?> t = iterationVariableTypes.get(i);
6302             if (init.get(i) == null) {
6303                 init.set(i, empty(methodType(t, commonSuffix)));
6304             }
6305             if (step.get(i) == null) {
6306                 step.set(i, dropArgumentsToMatch(identityOrVoid(t), 0, commonParameterSequence, i));
6307             }
6308             if (pred.get(i) == null) {
6309                 pred.set(i, dropArguments0(constant(boolean.class, true), 0, commonParameterSequence));
6310             }
6311             if (fini.get(i) == null) {
6312                 fini.set(i, empty(methodType(t, commonParameterSequence)));
6313             }
6314         }
6315 
6316         // Step 4: fill in missing parameter types.
6317         // Also convert all handles to fixed-arity handles.
6318         List<MethodHandle> finit = fixArities(fillParameterTypes(init, commonSuffix));
6319         List<MethodHandle> fstep = fixArities(fillParameterTypes(step, commonParameterSequence));
6320         List<MethodHandle> fpred = fixArities(fillParameterTypes(pred, commonParameterSequence));
6321         List<MethodHandle> ffini = fixArities(fillParameterTypes(fini, commonParameterSequence));
6322 
6323         assert finit.stream().map(MethodHandle::type).map(MethodType::parameterList).
6324                 allMatch(pl -> pl.equals(commonSuffix));
6325         assert Stream.of(fstep, fpred, ffini).flatMap(List::stream).map(MethodHandle::type).map(MethodType::parameterList).
6326                 allMatch(pl -> pl.equals(commonParameterSequence));
6327 
6328         return MethodHandleImpl.makeLoop(loopReturnType, commonSuffix, finit, fstep, fpred, ffini);
6329     }
6330 
6331     private static void loopChecks0(MethodHandle[][] clauses) {
6332         if (clauses == null || clauses.length == 0) {
6333             throw newIllegalArgumentException("null or no clauses passed");
6334         }
6335         if (Stream.of(clauses).anyMatch(Objects::isNull)) {
6336             throw newIllegalArgumentException("null clauses are not allowed");
6337         }
6338         if (Stream.of(clauses).anyMatch(c -> c.length > 4)) {
6339             throw newIllegalArgumentException("All loop clauses must be represented as MethodHandle arrays with at most 4 elements.");
6340         }
6341     }
6342 
6343     private static void loopChecks1a(int i, MethodHandle in, MethodHandle st) {
6344         if (in.type().returnType() != st.type().returnType()) {
6345             throw misMatchedTypes("clause " + i + ": init and step return types", in.type().returnType(),
6346                     st.type().returnType());
6347         }
6348     }
6349 
6350     private static List<Class<?>> longestParameterList(Stream<MethodHandle> mhs, int skipSize) {
6351         final List<Class<?>> empty = List.of();
6352         final List<Class<?>> longest = mhs.filter(Objects::nonNull).
6353                 // take only those that can contribute to a common suffix because they are longer than the prefix
6354                         map(MethodHandle::type).
6355                         filter(t -> t.parameterCount() > skipSize).
6356                         map(MethodType::parameterList).
6357                         reduce((p, q) -> p.size() >= q.size() ? p : q).orElse(empty);
6358         return longest.size() == 0 ? empty : longest.subList(skipSize, longest.size());
6359     }
6360 
6361     private static List<Class<?>> longestParameterList(List<List<Class<?>>> lists) {
6362         final List<Class<?>> empty = List.of();
6363         return lists.stream().reduce((p, q) -> p.size() >= q.size() ? p : q).orElse(empty);
6364     }
6365 
6366     private static List<Class<?>> buildCommonSuffix(List<MethodHandle> init, List<MethodHandle> step, List<MethodHandle> pred, List<MethodHandle> fini, int cpSize) {
6367         final List<Class<?>> longest1 = longestParameterList(Stream.of(step, pred, fini).flatMap(List::stream), cpSize);
6368         final List<Class<?>> longest2 = longestParameterList(init.stream(), 0);
6369         return longestParameterList(Arrays.asList(longest1, longest2));
6370     }
6371 
6372     private static void loopChecks1b(List<MethodHandle> init, List<Class<?>> commonSuffix) {
6373         if (init.stream().filter(Objects::nonNull).map(MethodHandle::type).
6374                 anyMatch(t -> !t.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, commonSuffix))) {
6375             throw newIllegalArgumentException("found non-effectively identical init parameter type lists: " + init +
6376                     " (common suffix: " + commonSuffix + ")");
6377         }
6378     }
6379 
6380     private static void loopChecks1cd(List<MethodHandle> pred, List<MethodHandle> fini, Class<?> loopReturnType) {
6381         if (fini.stream().filter(Objects::nonNull).map(MethodHandle::type).map(MethodType::returnType).
6382                 anyMatch(t -> t != loopReturnType)) {
6383             throw newIllegalArgumentException("found non-identical finalizer return types: " + fini + " (return type: " +
6384                     loopReturnType + ")");
6385         }
6386 
6387         if (!pred.stream().filter(Objects::nonNull).findFirst().isPresent()) {
6388             throw newIllegalArgumentException("no predicate found", pred);
6389         }
6390         if (pred.stream().filter(Objects::nonNull).map(MethodHandle::type).map(MethodType::returnType).
6391                 anyMatch(t -> t != boolean.class)) {
6392             throw newIllegalArgumentException("predicates must have boolean return type", pred);
6393         }
6394     }
6395 
6396     private static void loopChecks2(List<MethodHandle> step, List<MethodHandle> pred, List<MethodHandle> fini, List<Class<?>> commonParameterSequence) {
6397         if (Stream.of(step, pred, fini).flatMap(List::stream).filter(Objects::nonNull).map(MethodHandle::type).
6398                 anyMatch(t -> !t.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, commonParameterSequence))) {
6399             throw newIllegalArgumentException("found non-effectively identical parameter type lists:\nstep: " + step +
6400                     "\npred: " + pred + "\nfini: " + fini + " (common parameter sequence: " + commonParameterSequence + ")");
6401         }
6402     }
6403 
6404     private static List<MethodHandle> fillParameterTypes(List<MethodHandle> hs, final List<Class<?>> targetParams) {
6405         return hs.stream().map(h -> {
6406             int pc = h.type().parameterCount();
6407             int tpsize = targetParams.size();
6408             return pc < tpsize ? dropArguments0(h, pc, targetParams.subList(pc, tpsize)) : h;
6409         }).collect(Collectors.toList());
6410     }
6411 
6412     private static List<MethodHandle> fixArities(List<MethodHandle> hs) {
6413         return hs.stream().map(MethodHandle::asFixedArity).collect(Collectors.toList());
6414     }
6415 
6416     /**
6417      * Constructs a {@code while} loop from an initializer, a body, and a predicate.
6418      * This is a convenience wrapper for the {@linkplain #loop(MethodHandle[][]) generic loop combinator}.
6419      * <p>
6420      * The {@code pred} handle describes the loop condition; and {@code body}, its body. The loop resulting from this
6421      * method will, in each iteration, first evaluate the predicate and then execute its body (if the predicate
6422      * evaluates to {@code true}).
6423      * The loop will terminate once the predicate evaluates to {@code false} (the body will not be executed in this case).
6424      * <p>
6425      * The {@code init} handle describes the initial value of an additional optional loop-local variable.
6426      * In each iteration, this loop-local variable, if present, will be passed to the {@code body}
6427      * and updated with the value returned from its invocation. The result of loop execution will be
6428      * the final value of the additional loop-local variable (if present).
6429      * <p>
6430      * The following rules hold for these argument handles:<ul>
6431      * <li>The {@code body} handle must not be {@code null}; its type must be of the form
6432      * {@code (V A...)V}, where {@code V} is non-{@code void}, or else {@code (A...)void}.
6433      * (In the {@code void} case, we assign the type {@code void} to the name {@code V},
6434      * and we will write {@code (V A...)V} with the understanding that a {@code void} type {@code V}
6435      * is quietly dropped from the parameter list, leaving {@code (A...)V}.)
6436      * <li>The parameter list {@code (V A...)} of the body is called the <em>internal parameter list</em>.
6437      * It will constrain the parameter lists of the other loop parts.
6438      * <li>If the iteration variable type {@code V} is dropped from the internal parameter list, the resulting shorter
6439      * list {@code (A...)} is called the <em>external parameter list</em>.
6440      * <li>The body return type {@code V}, if non-{@code void}, determines the type of an
6441      * additional state variable of the loop.
6442      * The body must both accept and return a value of this type {@code V}.
6443      * <li>If {@code init} is non-{@code null}, it must have return type {@code V}.
6444      * Its parameter list (of some <a href="MethodHandles.html#astar">form {@code (A*)}</a>) must be
6445      * <a href="MethodHandles.html#effid">effectively identical</a>
6446      * to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6447      * <li>If {@code init} is {@code null}, the loop variable will be initialized to its
6448      * {@linkplain #empty default value}.
6449      * <li>The {@code pred} handle must not be {@code null}.  It must have {@code boolean} as its return type.
6450      * Its parameter list (either empty or of the form {@code (V A*)}) must be
6451      * effectively identical to the internal parameter list.
6452      * </ul>
6453      * <p>
6454      * The resulting loop handle's result type and parameter signature are determined as follows:<ul>
6455      * <li>The loop handle's result type is the result type {@code V} of the body.
6456      * <li>The loop handle's parameter types are the types {@code (A...)},
6457      * from the external parameter list.
6458      * </ul>
6459      * <p>
6460      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. In the code, {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type / value of
6461      * the sole loop variable as well as the result type of the loop; and {@code A}/{@code a}, that of the argument
6462      * passed to the loop.
6463      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6464      * V init(A...);
6465      * boolean pred(V, A...);
6466      * V body(V, A...);
6467      * V whileLoop(A... a...) {
6468      *   V v = init(a...);
6469      *   while (pred(v, a...)) {
6470      *     v = body(v, a...);
6471      *   }
6472      *   return v;
6473      * }
6474      * }</pre></blockquote>
6475      *
6476      * @apiNote Example:
6477      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6478      * // implement the zip function for lists as a loop handle
6479      * static List<String> initZip(Iterator<String> a, Iterator<String> b) { return new ArrayList<>(); }
6480      * static boolean zipPred(List<String> zip, Iterator<String> a, Iterator<String> b) { return a.hasNext() && b.hasNext(); }
6481      * static List<String> zipStep(List<String> zip, Iterator<String> a, Iterator<String> b) {
6482      *   zip.add(a.next());
6483      *   zip.add(b.next());
6484      *   return zip;
6485      * }
6486      * // assume MH_initZip, MH_zipPred, and MH_zipStep are handles to the above methods
6487      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.whileLoop(MH_initZip, MH_zipPred, MH_zipStep);
6488      * List<String> a = Arrays.asList("a", "b", "c", "d");
6489      * List<String> b = Arrays.asList("e", "f", "g", "h");
6490      * List<String> zipped = Arrays.asList("a", "e", "b", "f", "c", "g", "d", "h");
6491      * assertEquals(zipped, (List<String>) loop.invoke(a.iterator(), b.iterator()));
6492      * }</pre></blockquote>
6493      *
6494      *
6495      * @apiNote The implementation of this method can be expressed as follows:
6496      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6497      * MethodHandle whileLoop(MethodHandle init, MethodHandle pred, MethodHandle body) {
6498      *     MethodHandle fini = (body.type().returnType() == void.class
6499      *                         ? null : identity(body.type().returnType()));
6500      *     MethodHandle[]
6501      *         checkExit = { null, null, pred, fini },
6502      *         varBody   = { init, body };
6503      *     return loop(checkExit, varBody);
6504      * }
6505      * }</pre></blockquote>
6506      *
6507      * @param init optional initializer, providing the initial value of the loop variable.
6508      *             May be {@code null}, implying a default initial value.  See above for other constraints.
6509      * @param pred condition for the loop, which may not be {@code null}. Its result type must be {@code boolean}. See
6510      *             above for other constraints.
6511      * @param body body of the loop, which may not be {@code null}. It controls the loop parameters and result type.
6512      *             See above for other constraints.
6513      *
6514      * @return a method handle implementing the {@code while} loop as described by the arguments.
6515      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the rules for the arguments are violated.
6516      * @throws NullPointerException if {@code pred} or {@code body} are {@code null}.
6517      *
6518      * @see #loop(MethodHandle[][])
6519      * @see #doWhileLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6520      * @since 9
6521      */
6522     public static MethodHandle whileLoop(MethodHandle init, MethodHandle pred, MethodHandle body) {
6523         whileLoopChecks(init, pred, body);
6524         MethodHandle fini = identityOrVoid(body.type().returnType());
6525         MethodHandle[] checkExit = { null, null, pred, fini };
6526         MethodHandle[] varBody = { init, body };
6527         return loop(checkExit, varBody);
6528     }
6529 
6530     /**
6531      * Constructs a {@code do-while} loop from an initializer, a body, and a predicate.
6532      * This is a convenience wrapper for the {@linkplain #loop(MethodHandle[][]) generic loop combinator}.
6533      * <p>
6534      * The {@code pred} handle describes the loop condition; and {@code body}, its body. The loop resulting from this
6535      * method will, in each iteration, first execute its body and then evaluate the predicate.
6536      * The loop will terminate once the predicate evaluates to {@code false} after an execution of the body.
6537      * <p>
6538      * The {@code init} handle describes the initial value of an additional optional loop-local variable.
6539      * In each iteration, this loop-local variable, if present, will be passed to the {@code body}
6540      * and updated with the value returned from its invocation. The result of loop execution will be
6541      * the final value of the additional loop-local variable (if present).
6542      * <p>
6543      * The following rules hold for these argument handles:<ul>
6544      * <li>The {@code body} handle must not be {@code null}; its type must be of the form
6545      * {@code (V A...)V}, where {@code V} is non-{@code void}, or else {@code (A...)void}.
6546      * (In the {@code void} case, we assign the type {@code void} to the name {@code V},
6547      * and we will write {@code (V A...)V} with the understanding that a {@code void} type {@code V}
6548      * is quietly dropped from the parameter list, leaving {@code (A...)V}.)
6549      * <li>The parameter list {@code (V A...)} of the body is called the <em>internal parameter list</em>.
6550      * It will constrain the parameter lists of the other loop parts.
6551      * <li>If the iteration variable type {@code V} is dropped from the internal parameter list, the resulting shorter
6552      * list {@code (A...)} is called the <em>external parameter list</em>.
6553      * <li>The body return type {@code V}, if non-{@code void}, determines the type of an
6554      * additional state variable of the loop.
6555      * The body must both accept and return a value of this type {@code V}.
6556      * <li>If {@code init} is non-{@code null}, it must have return type {@code V}.
6557      * Its parameter list (of some <a href="MethodHandles.html#astar">form {@code (A*)}</a>) must be
6558      * <a href="MethodHandles.html#effid">effectively identical</a>
6559      * to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6560      * <li>If {@code init} is {@code null}, the loop variable will be initialized to its
6561      * {@linkplain #empty default value}.
6562      * <li>The {@code pred} handle must not be {@code null}.  It must have {@code boolean} as its return type.
6563      * Its parameter list (either empty or of the form {@code (V A*)}) must be
6564      * effectively identical to the internal parameter list.
6565      * </ul>
6566      * <p>
6567      * The resulting loop handle's result type and parameter signature are determined as follows:<ul>
6568      * <li>The loop handle's result type is the result type {@code V} of the body.
6569      * <li>The loop handle's parameter types are the types {@code (A...)},
6570      * from the external parameter list.
6571      * </ul>
6572      * <p>
6573      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. In the code, {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type / value of
6574      * the sole loop variable as well as the result type of the loop; and {@code A}/{@code a}, that of the argument
6575      * passed to the loop.
6576      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6577      * V init(A...);
6578      * boolean pred(V, A...);
6579      * V body(V, A...);
6580      * V doWhileLoop(A... a...) {
6581      *   V v = init(a...);
6582      *   do {
6583      *     v = body(v, a...);
6584      *   } while (pred(v, a...));
6585      *   return v;
6586      * }
6587      * }</pre></blockquote>
6588      *
6589      * @apiNote Example:
6590      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6591      * // int i = 0; while (i < limit) { ++i; } return i; => limit
6592      * static int zero(int limit) { return 0; }
6593      * static int step(int i, int limit) { return i + 1; }
6594      * static boolean pred(int i, int limit) { return i < limit; }
6595      * // assume MH_zero, MH_step, and MH_pred are handles to the above methods
6596      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.doWhileLoop(MH_zero, MH_step, MH_pred);
6597      * assertEquals(23, loop.invoke(23));
6598      * }</pre></blockquote>
6599      *
6600      *
6601      * @apiNote The implementation of this method can be expressed as follows:
6602      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6603      * MethodHandle doWhileLoop(MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body, MethodHandle pred) {
6604      *     MethodHandle fini = (body.type().returnType() == void.class
6605      *                         ? null : identity(body.type().returnType()));
6606      *     MethodHandle[] clause = { init, body, pred, fini };
6607      *     return loop(clause);
6608      * }
6609      * }</pre></blockquote>
6610      *
6611      * @param init optional initializer, providing the initial value of the loop variable.
6612      *             May be {@code null}, implying a default initial value.  See above for other constraints.
6613      * @param body body of the loop, which may not be {@code null}. It controls the loop parameters and result type.
6614      *             See above for other constraints.
6615      * @param pred condition for the loop, which may not be {@code null}. Its result type must be {@code boolean}. See
6616      *             above for other constraints.
6617      *
6618      * @return a method handle implementing the {@code while} loop as described by the arguments.
6619      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the rules for the arguments are violated.
6620      * @throws NullPointerException if {@code pred} or {@code body} are {@code null}.
6621      *
6622      * @see #loop(MethodHandle[][])
6623      * @see #whileLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6624      * @since 9
6625      */
6626     public static MethodHandle doWhileLoop(MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body, MethodHandle pred) {
6627         whileLoopChecks(init, pred, body);
6628         MethodHandle fini = identityOrVoid(body.type().returnType());
6629         MethodHandle[] clause = {init, body, pred, fini };
6630         return loop(clause);
6631     }
6632 
6633     private static void whileLoopChecks(MethodHandle init, MethodHandle pred, MethodHandle body) {
6634         Objects.requireNonNull(pred);
6635         Objects.requireNonNull(body);
6636         MethodType bodyType = body.type();
6637         Class<?> returnType = bodyType.returnType();
6638         List<Class<?>> innerList = bodyType.parameterList();
6639         List<Class<?>> outerList = innerList;
6640         if (returnType == void.class) {
6641             // OK
6642         } else if (innerList.size() == 0 || innerList.get(0) != returnType) {
6643             // leading V argument missing => error
6644             MethodType expected = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(0, returnType);
6645             throw misMatchedTypes("body function", bodyType, expected);
6646         } else {
6647             outerList = innerList.subList(1, innerList.size());
6648         }
6649         MethodType predType = pred.type();
6650         if (predType.returnType() != boolean.class ||
6651                 !predType.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, innerList)) {
6652             throw misMatchedTypes("loop predicate", predType, methodType(boolean.class, innerList));
6653         }
6654         if (init != null) {
6655             MethodType initType = init.type();
6656             if (initType.returnType() != returnType ||
6657                     !initType.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, outerList)) {
6658                 throw misMatchedTypes("loop initializer", initType, methodType(returnType, outerList));
6659             }
6660         }
6661     }
6662 
6663     /**
6664      * Constructs a loop that runs a given number of iterations.
6665      * This is a convenience wrapper for the {@linkplain #loop(MethodHandle[][]) generic loop combinator}.
6666      * <p>
6667      * The number of iterations is determined by the {@code iterations} handle evaluation result.
6668      * The loop counter {@code i} is an extra loop iteration variable of type {@code int}.
6669      * It will be initialized to 0 and incremented by 1 in each iteration.
6670      * <p>
6671      * If the {@code body} handle returns a non-{@code void} type {@code V}, a leading loop iteration variable
6672      * of that type is also present.  This variable is initialized using the optional {@code init} handle,
6673      * or to the {@linkplain #empty default value} of type {@code V} if that handle is {@code null}.
6674      * <p>
6675      * In each iteration, the iteration variables are passed to an invocation of the {@code body} handle.
6676      * A non-{@code void} value returned from the body (of type {@code V}) updates the leading
6677      * iteration variable.
6678      * The result of the loop handle execution will be the final {@code V} value of that variable
6679      * (or {@code void} if there is no {@code V} variable).
6680      * <p>
6681      * The following rules hold for the argument handles:<ul>
6682      * <li>The {@code iterations} handle must not be {@code null}, and must return
6683      * the type {@code int}, referred to here as {@code I} in parameter type lists.
6684      * <li>The {@code body} handle must not be {@code null}; its type must be of the form
6685      * {@code (V I A...)V}, where {@code V} is non-{@code void}, or else {@code (I A...)void}.
6686      * (In the {@code void} case, we assign the type {@code void} to the name {@code V},
6687      * and we will write {@code (V I A...)V} with the understanding that a {@code void} type {@code V}
6688      * is quietly dropped from the parameter list, leaving {@code (I A...)V}.)
6689      * <li>The parameter list {@code (V I A...)} of the body contributes to a list
6690      * of types called the <em>internal parameter list</em>.
6691      * It will constrain the parameter lists of the other loop parts.
6692      * <li>As a special case, if the body contributes only {@code V} and {@code I} types,
6693      * with no additional {@code A} types, then the internal parameter list is extended by
6694      * the argument types {@code A...} of the {@code iterations} handle.
6695      * <li>If the iteration variable types {@code (V I)} are dropped from the internal parameter list, the resulting shorter
6696      * list {@code (A...)} is called the <em>external parameter list</em>.
6697      * <li>The body return type {@code V}, if non-{@code void}, determines the type of an
6698      * additional state variable of the loop.
6699      * The body must both accept a leading parameter and return a value of this type {@code V}.
6700      * <li>If {@code init} is non-{@code null}, it must have return type {@code V}.
6701      * Its parameter list (of some <a href="MethodHandles.html#astar">form {@code (A*)}</a>) must be
6702      * <a href="MethodHandles.html#effid">effectively identical</a>
6703      * to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6704      * <li>If {@code init} is {@code null}, the loop variable will be initialized to its
6705      * {@linkplain #empty default value}.
6706      * <li>The parameter list of {@code iterations} (of some form {@code (A*)}) must be
6707      * effectively identical to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6708      * </ul>
6709      * <p>
6710      * The resulting loop handle's result type and parameter signature are determined as follows:<ul>
6711      * <li>The loop handle's result type is the result type {@code V} of the body.
6712      * <li>The loop handle's parameter types are the types {@code (A...)},
6713      * from the external parameter list.
6714      * </ul>
6715      * <p>
6716      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. In the code, {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type / value of
6717      * the second loop variable as well as the result type of the loop; and {@code A...}/{@code a...} represent
6718      * arguments passed to the loop.
6719      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6720      * int iterations(A...);
6721      * V init(A...);
6722      * V body(V, int, A...);
6723      * V countedLoop(A... a...) {
6724      *   int end = iterations(a...);
6725      *   V v = init(a...);
6726      *   for (int i = 0; i < end; ++i) {
6727      *     v = body(v, i, a...);
6728      *   }
6729      *   return v;
6730      * }
6731      * }</pre></blockquote>
6732      *
6733      * @apiNote Example with a fully conformant body method:
6734      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6735      * // String s = "Lambdaman!"; for (int i = 0; i < 13; ++i) { s = "na " + s; } return s;
6736      * // => a variation on a well known theme
6737      * static String step(String v, int counter, String init) { return "na " + v; }
6738      * // assume MH_step is a handle to the method above
6739      * MethodHandle fit13 = MethodHandles.constant(int.class, 13);
6740      * MethodHandle start = MethodHandles.identity(String.class);
6741      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.countedLoop(fit13, start, MH_step);
6742      * assertEquals("na na na na na na na na na na na na na Lambdaman!", loop.invoke("Lambdaman!"));
6743      * }</pre></blockquote>
6744      *
6745      * @apiNote Example with the simplest possible body method type,
6746      * and passing the number of iterations to the loop invocation:
6747      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6748      * // String s = "Lambdaman!"; for (int i = 0; i < 13; ++i) { s = "na " + s; } return s;
6749      * // => a variation on a well known theme
6750      * static String step(String v, int counter ) { return "na " + v; }
6751      * // assume MH_step is a handle to the method above
6752      * MethodHandle count = MethodHandles.dropArguments(MethodHandles.identity(int.class), 1, String.class);
6753      * MethodHandle start = MethodHandles.dropArguments(MethodHandles.identity(String.class), 0, int.class);
6754      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.countedLoop(count, start, MH_step);  // (v, i) -> "na " + v
6755      * assertEquals("na na na na na na na na na na na na na Lambdaman!", loop.invoke(13, "Lambdaman!"));
6756      * }</pre></blockquote>
6757      *
6758      * @apiNote Example that treats the number of iterations, string to append to, and string to append
6759      * as loop parameters:
6760      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6761      * // String s = "Lambdaman!", t = "na"; for (int i = 0; i < 13; ++i) { s = t + " " + s; } return s;
6762      * // => a variation on a well known theme
6763      * static String step(String v, int counter, int iterations_, String pre, String start_) { return pre + " " + v; }
6764      * // assume MH_step is a handle to the method above
6765      * MethodHandle count = MethodHandles.identity(int.class);
6766      * MethodHandle start = MethodHandles.dropArguments(MethodHandles.identity(String.class), 0, int.class, String.class);
6767      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.countedLoop(count, start, MH_step);  // (v, i, _, pre, _) -> pre + " " + v
6768      * assertEquals("na na na na na na na na na na na na na Lambdaman!", loop.invoke(13, "na", "Lambdaman!"));
6769      * }</pre></blockquote>
6770      *
6771      * @apiNote Example that illustrates the usage of {@link #dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandle, int, List, int)}
6772      * to enforce a loop type:
6773      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6774      * // String s = "Lambdaman!", t = "na"; for (int i = 0; i < 13; ++i) { s = t + " " + s; } return s;
6775      * // => a variation on a well known theme
6776      * static String step(String v, int counter, String pre) { return pre + " " + v; }
6777      * // assume MH_step is a handle to the method above
6778      * MethodType loopType = methodType(String.class, String.class, int.class, String.class);
6779      * MethodHandle count = MethodHandles.dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandles.identity(int.class),    0, loopType.parameterList(), 1);
6780      * MethodHandle start = MethodHandles.dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandles.identity(String.class), 0, loopType.parameterList(), 2);
6781      * MethodHandle body  = MethodHandles.dropArgumentsToMatch(MH_step,                              2, loopType.parameterList(), 0);
6782      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.countedLoop(count, start, body);  // (v, i, pre, _, _) -> pre + " " + v
6783      * assertEquals("na na na na na na na na na na na na na Lambdaman!", loop.invoke("na", 13, "Lambdaman!"));
6784      * }</pre></blockquote>
6785      *
6786      * @apiNote The implementation of this method can be expressed as follows:
6787      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6788      * MethodHandle countedLoop(MethodHandle iterations, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
6789      *     return countedLoop(empty(iterations.type()), iterations, init, body);
6790      * }
6791      * }</pre></blockquote>
6792      *
6793      * @param iterations a non-{@code null} handle to return the number of iterations this loop should run. The handle's
6794      *                   result type must be {@code int}. See above for other constraints.
6795      * @param init optional initializer, providing the initial value of the loop variable.
6796      *             May be {@code null}, implying a default initial value.  See above for other constraints.
6797      * @param body body of the loop, which may not be {@code null}.
6798      *             It controls the loop parameters and result type in the standard case (see above for details).
6799      *             It must accept its own return type (if non-void) plus an {@code int} parameter (for the counter),
6800      *             and may accept any number of additional types.
6801      *             See above for other constraints.
6802      *
6803      * @return a method handle representing the loop.
6804      * @throws NullPointerException if either of the {@code iterations} or {@code body} handles is {@code null}.
6805      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if any argument violates the rules formulated above.
6806      *
6807      * @see #countedLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6808      * @since 9
6809      */
6810     public static MethodHandle countedLoop(MethodHandle iterations, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
6811         return countedLoop(empty(iterations.type()), iterations, init, body);
6812     }
6813 
6814     /**
6815      * Constructs a loop that counts over a range of numbers.
6816      * This is a convenience wrapper for the {@linkplain #loop(MethodHandle[][]) generic loop combinator}.
6817      * <p>
6818      * The loop counter {@code i} is a loop iteration variable of type {@code int}.
6819      * The {@code start} and {@code end} handles determine the start (inclusive) and end (exclusive)
6820      * values of the loop counter.
6821      * The loop counter will be initialized to the {@code int} value returned from the evaluation of the
6822      * {@code start} handle and run to the value returned from {@code end} (exclusively) with a step width of 1.
6823      * <p>
6824      * If the {@code body} handle returns a non-{@code void} type {@code V}, a leading loop iteration variable
6825      * of that type is also present.  This variable is initialized using the optional {@code init} handle,
6826      * or to the {@linkplain #empty default value} of type {@code V} if that handle is {@code null}.
6827      * <p>
6828      * In each iteration, the iteration variables are passed to an invocation of the {@code body} handle.
6829      * A non-{@code void} value returned from the body (of type {@code V}) updates the leading
6830      * iteration variable.
6831      * The result of the loop handle execution will be the final {@code V} value of that variable
6832      * (or {@code void} if there is no {@code V} variable).
6833      * <p>
6834      * The following rules hold for the argument handles:<ul>
6835      * <li>The {@code start} and {@code end} handles must not be {@code null}, and must both return
6836      * the common type {@code int}, referred to here as {@code I} in parameter type lists.
6837      * <li>The {@code body} handle must not be {@code null}; its type must be of the form
6838      * {@code (V I A...)V}, where {@code V} is non-{@code void}, or else {@code (I A...)void}.
6839      * (In the {@code void} case, we assign the type {@code void} to the name {@code V},
6840      * and we will write {@code (V I A...)V} with the understanding that a {@code void} type {@code V}
6841      * is quietly dropped from the parameter list, leaving {@code (I A...)V}.)
6842      * <li>The parameter list {@code (V I A...)} of the body contributes to a list
6843      * of types called the <em>internal parameter list</em>.
6844      * It will constrain the parameter lists of the other loop parts.
6845      * <li>As a special case, if the body contributes only {@code V} and {@code I} types,
6846      * with no additional {@code A} types, then the internal parameter list is extended by
6847      * the argument types {@code A...} of the {@code end} handle.
6848      * <li>If the iteration variable types {@code (V I)} are dropped from the internal parameter list, the resulting shorter
6849      * list {@code (A...)} is called the <em>external parameter list</em>.
6850      * <li>The body return type {@code V}, if non-{@code void}, determines the type of an
6851      * additional state variable of the loop.
6852      * The body must both accept a leading parameter and return a value of this type {@code V}.
6853      * <li>If {@code init} is non-{@code null}, it must have return type {@code V}.
6854      * Its parameter list (of some <a href="MethodHandles.html#astar">form {@code (A*)}</a>) must be
6855      * <a href="MethodHandles.html#effid">effectively identical</a>
6856      * to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6857      * <li>If {@code init} is {@code null}, the loop variable will be initialized to its
6858      * {@linkplain #empty default value}.
6859      * <li>The parameter list of {@code start} (of some form {@code (A*)}) must be
6860      * effectively identical to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6861      * <li>Likewise, the parameter list of {@code end} must be effectively identical
6862      * to the external parameter list.
6863      * </ul>
6864      * <p>
6865      * The resulting loop handle's result type and parameter signature are determined as follows:<ul>
6866      * <li>The loop handle's result type is the result type {@code V} of the body.
6867      * <li>The loop handle's parameter types are the types {@code (A...)},
6868      * from the external parameter list.
6869      * </ul>
6870      * <p>
6871      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. In the code, {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type / value of
6872      * the second loop variable as well as the result type of the loop; and {@code A...}/{@code a...} represent
6873      * arguments passed to the loop.
6874      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6875      * int start(A...);
6876      * int end(A...);
6877      * V init(A...);
6878      * V body(V, int, A...);
6879      * V countedLoop(A... a...) {
6880      *   int e = end(a...);
6881      *   int s = start(a...);
6882      *   V v = init(a...);
6883      *   for (int i = s; i < e; ++i) {
6884      *     v = body(v, i, a...);
6885      *   }
6886      *   return v;
6887      * }
6888      * }</pre></blockquote>
6889      *
6890      * @apiNote The implementation of this method can be expressed as follows:
6891      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6892      * MethodHandle countedLoop(MethodHandle start, MethodHandle end, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
6893      *     MethodHandle returnVar = dropArguments(identity(init.type().returnType()), 0, int.class, int.class);
6894      *     // assume MH_increment and MH_predicate are handles to implementation-internal methods with
6895      *     // the following semantics:
6896      *     // MH_increment: (int limit, int counter) -> counter + 1
6897      *     // MH_predicate: (int limit, int counter) -> counter < limit
6898      *     Class<?> counterType = start.type().returnType();  // int
6899      *     Class<?> returnType = body.type().returnType();
6900      *     MethodHandle incr = MH_increment, pred = MH_predicate, retv = null;
6901      *     if (returnType != void.class) {  // ignore the V variable
6902      *         incr = dropArguments(incr, 1, returnType);  // (limit, v, i) => (limit, i)
6903      *         pred = dropArguments(pred, 1, returnType);  // ditto
6904      *         retv = dropArguments(identity(returnType), 0, counterType); // ignore limit
6905      *     }
6906      *     body = dropArguments(body, 0, counterType);  // ignore the limit variable
6907      *     MethodHandle[]
6908      *         loopLimit  = { end, null, pred, retv }, // limit = end(); i < limit || return v
6909      *         bodyClause = { init, body },            // v = init(); v = body(v, i)
6910      *         indexVar   = { start, incr };           // i = start(); i = i + 1
6911      *     return loop(loopLimit, bodyClause, indexVar);
6912      * }
6913      * }</pre></blockquote>
6914      *
6915      * @param start a non-{@code null} handle to return the start value of the loop counter, which must be {@code int}.
6916      *              See above for other constraints.
6917      * @param end a non-{@code null} handle to return the end value of the loop counter (the loop will run to
6918      *            {@code end-1}). The result type must be {@code int}. See above for other constraints.
6919      * @param init optional initializer, providing the initial value of the loop variable.
6920      *             May be {@code null}, implying a default initial value.  See above for other constraints.
6921      * @param body body of the loop, which may not be {@code null}.
6922      *             It controls the loop parameters and result type in the standard case (see above for details).
6923      *             It must accept its own return type (if non-void) plus an {@code int} parameter (for the counter),
6924      *             and may accept any number of additional types.
6925      *             See above for other constraints.
6926      *
6927      * @return a method handle representing the loop.
6928      * @throws NullPointerException if any of the {@code start}, {@code end}, or {@code body} handles is {@code null}.
6929      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if any argument violates the rules formulated above.
6930      *
6931      * @see #countedLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6932      * @since 9
6933      */
6934     public static MethodHandle countedLoop(MethodHandle start, MethodHandle end, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
6935         countedLoopChecks(start, end, init, body);
6936         Class<?> counterType = start.type().returnType();  // int, but who's counting?
6937         Class<?> limitType   = end.type().returnType();    // yes, int again
6938         Class<?> returnType  = body.type().returnType();
6939         MethodHandle incr = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_countedLoopStep);
6940         MethodHandle pred = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_countedLoopPred);
6941         MethodHandle retv = null;
6942         if (returnType != void.class) {
6943             incr = dropArguments(incr, 1, returnType);  // (limit, v, i) => (limit, i)
6944             pred = dropArguments(pred, 1, returnType);  // ditto
6945             retv = dropArguments(identity(returnType), 0, counterType);
6946         }
6947         body = dropArguments(body, 0, counterType);  // ignore the limit variable
6948         MethodHandle[]
6949             loopLimit  = { end, null, pred, retv }, // limit = end(); i < limit || return v
6950             bodyClause = { init, body },            // v = init(); v = body(v, i)
6951             indexVar   = { start, incr };           // i = start(); i = i + 1
6952         return loop(loopLimit, bodyClause, indexVar);
6953     }
6954 
6955     private static void countedLoopChecks(MethodHandle start, MethodHandle end, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
6956         Objects.requireNonNull(start);
6957         Objects.requireNonNull(end);
6958         Objects.requireNonNull(body);
6959         Class<?> counterType = start.type().returnType();
6960         if (counterType != int.class) {
6961             MethodType expected = start.type().changeReturnType(int.class);
6962             throw misMatchedTypes("start function", start.type(), expected);
6963         } else if (end.type().returnType() != counterType) {
6964             MethodType expected = end.type().changeReturnType(counterType);
6965             throw misMatchedTypes("end function", end.type(), expected);
6966         }
6967         MethodType bodyType = body.type();
6968         Class<?> returnType = bodyType.returnType();
6969         List<Class<?>> innerList = bodyType.parameterList();
6970         // strip leading V value if present
6971         int vsize = (returnType == void.class ? 0 : 1);
6972         if (vsize != 0 && (innerList.size() == 0 || innerList.get(0) != returnType)) {
6973             // argument list has no "V" => error
6974             MethodType expected = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(0, returnType);
6975             throw misMatchedTypes("body function", bodyType, expected);
6976         } else if (innerList.size() <= vsize || innerList.get(vsize) != counterType) {
6977             // missing I type => error
6978             MethodType expected = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(vsize, counterType);
6979             throw misMatchedTypes("body function", bodyType, expected);
6980         }
6981         List<Class<?>> outerList = innerList.subList(vsize + 1, innerList.size());
6982         if (outerList.isEmpty()) {
6983             // special case; take lists from end handle
6984             outerList = end.type().parameterList();
6985             innerList = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(vsize + 1, outerList).parameterList();
6986         }
6987         MethodType expected = methodType(counterType, outerList);
6988         if (!start.type().effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, outerList)) {
6989             throw misMatchedTypes("start parameter types", start.type(), expected);
6990         }
6991         if (end.type() != start.type() &&
6992             !end.type().effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, outerList)) {
6993             throw misMatchedTypes("end parameter types", end.type(), expected);
6994         }
6995         if (init != null) {
6996             MethodType initType = init.type();
6997             if (initType.returnType() != returnType ||
6998                 !initType.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, outerList)) {
6999                 throw misMatchedTypes("loop initializer", initType, methodType(returnType, outerList));
7000             }
7001         }
7002     }
7003 
7004     /**
7005      * Constructs a loop that ranges over the values produced by an {@code Iterator<T>}.
7006      * This is a convenience wrapper for the {@linkplain #loop(MethodHandle[][]) generic loop combinator}.
7007      * <p>
7008      * The iterator itself will be determined by the evaluation of the {@code iterator} handle.
7009      * Each value it produces will be stored in a loop iteration variable of type {@code T}.
7010      * <p>
7011      * If the {@code body} handle returns a non-{@code void} type {@code V}, a leading loop iteration variable
7012      * of that type is also present.  This variable is initialized using the optional {@code init} handle,
7013      * or to the {@linkplain #empty default value} of type {@code V} if that handle is {@code null}.
7014      * <p>
7015      * In each iteration, the iteration variables are passed to an invocation of the {@code body} handle.
7016      * A non-{@code void} value returned from the body (of type {@code V}) updates the leading
7017      * iteration variable.
7018      * The result of the loop handle execution will be the final {@code V} value of that variable
7019      * (or {@code void} if there is no {@code V} variable).
7020      * <p>
7021      * The following rules hold for the argument handles:<ul>
7022      * <li>The {@code body} handle must not be {@code null}; its type must be of the form
7023      * {@code (V T A...)V}, where {@code V} is non-{@code void}, or else {@code (T A...)void}.
7024      * (In the {@code void} case, we assign the type {@code void} to the name {@code V},
7025      * and we will write {@code (V T A...)V} with the understanding that a {@code void} type {@code V}
7026      * is quietly dropped from the parameter list, leaving {@code (T A...)V}.)
7027      * <li>The parameter list {@code (V T A...)} of the body contributes to a list
7028      * of types called the <em>internal parameter list</em>.
7029      * It will constrain the parameter lists of the other loop parts.
7030      * <li>As a special case, if the body contributes only {@code V} and {@code T} types,
7031      * with no additional {@code A} types, then the internal parameter list is extended by
7032      * the argument types {@code A...} of the {@code iterator} handle; if it is {@code null} the
7033      * single type {@code Iterable} is added and constitutes the {@code A...} list.
7034      * <li>If the iteration variable types {@code (V T)} are dropped from the internal parameter list, the resulting shorter
7035      * list {@code (A...)} is called the <em>external parameter list</em>.
7036      * <li>The body return type {@code V}, if non-{@code void}, determines the type of an
7037      * additional state variable of the loop.
7038      * The body must both accept a leading parameter and return a value of this type {@code V}.
7039      * <li>If {@code init} is non-{@code null}, it must have return type {@code V}.
7040      * Its parameter list (of some <a href="MethodHandles.html#astar">form {@code (A*)}</a>) must be
7041      * <a href="MethodHandles.html#effid">effectively identical</a>
7042      * to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
7043      * <li>If {@code init} is {@code null}, the loop variable will be initialized to its
7044      * {@linkplain #empty default value}.
7045      * <li>If the {@code iterator} handle is non-{@code null}, it must have the return
7046      * type {@code java.util.Iterator} or a subtype thereof.
7047      * The iterator it produces when the loop is executed will be assumed
7048      * to yield values which can be converted to type {@code T}.
7049      * <li>The parameter list of an {@code iterator} that is non-{@code null} (of some form {@code (A*)}) must be
7050      * effectively identical to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
7051      * <li>If {@code iterator} is {@code null} it defaults to a method handle which behaves
7052      * like {@link java.lang.Iterable#iterator()}.  In that case, the internal parameter list
7053      * {@code (V T A...)} must have at least one {@code A} type, and the default iterator
7054      * handle parameter is adjusted to accept the leading {@code A} type, as if by
7055      * the {@link MethodHandle#asType asType} conversion method.
7056      * The leading {@code A} type must be {@code Iterable} or a subtype thereof.
7057      * This conversion step, done at loop construction time, must not throw a {@code WrongMethodTypeException}.
7058      * </ul>
7059      * <p>
7060      * The type {@code T} may be either a primitive or reference.
7061      * Since type {@code Iterator<T>} is erased in the method handle representation to the raw type {@code Iterator},
7062      * the {@code iteratedLoop} combinator adjusts the leading argument type for {@code body} to {@code Object}
7063      * as if by the {@link MethodHandle#asType asType} conversion method.
7064      * Therefore, if an iterator of the wrong type appears as the loop is executed, runtime exceptions may occur
7065      * as the result of dynamic conversions performed by {@link MethodHandle#asType(MethodType)}.
7066      * <p>
7067      * The resulting loop handle's result type and parameter signature are determined as follows:<ul>
7068      * <li>The loop handle's result type is the result type {@code V} of the body.
7069      * <li>The loop handle's parameter types are the types {@code (A...)},
7070      * from the external parameter list.
7071      * </ul>
7072      * <p>
7073      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. In the code, {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type / value of
7074      * the loop variable as well as the result type of the loop; {@code T}/{@code t}, that of the elements of the
7075      * structure the loop iterates over, and {@code A...}/{@code a...} represent arguments passed to the loop.
7076      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
7077      * Iterator<T> iterator(A...);  // defaults to Iterable::iterator
7078      * V init(A...);
7079      * V body(V,T,A...);
7080      * V iteratedLoop(A... a...) {
7081      *   Iterator<T> it = iterator(a...);
7082      *   V v = init(a...);
7083      *   while (it.hasNext()) {
7084      *     T t = it.next();
7085      *     v = body(v, t, a...);
7086      *   }
7087      *   return v;
7088      * }
7089      * }</pre></blockquote>
7090      *
7091      * @apiNote Example:
7092      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
7093      * // get an iterator from a list
7094      * static List<String> reverseStep(List<String> r, String e) {
7095      *   r.add(0, e);
7096      *   return r;
7097      * }
