7098      * static List<String> newArrayList() { return new ArrayList<>(); }
7099      * // assume MH_reverseStep and MH_newArrayList are handles to the above methods
7100      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.iteratedLoop(null, MH_newArrayList, MH_reverseStep);
7101      * List<String> list = Arrays.asList("a", "b", "c", "d", "e");
7102      * List<String> reversedList = Arrays.asList("e", "d", "c", "b", "a");
7103      * assertEquals(reversedList, (List<String>) loop.invoke(list));
7104      * }</pre></blockquote>
7105      *
7106      * @apiNote The implementation of this method can be expressed approximately as follows:
7107      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
7108      * MethodHandle iteratedLoop(MethodHandle iterator, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
7109      *     // assume MH_next, MH_hasNext, MH_startIter are handles to methods of Iterator/Iterable
7110      *     Class<?> returnType = body.type().returnType();
7111      *     Class<?> ttype = body.type().parameterType(returnType == void.class ? 0 : 1);
7112      *     MethodHandle nextVal = MH_next.asType(MH_next.type().changeReturnType(ttype));
7113      *     MethodHandle retv = null, step = body, startIter = iterator;
7114      *     if (returnType != void.class) {
7115      *         // the simple thing first:  in (I V A...), drop the I to get V
7116      *         retv = dropArguments(identity(returnType), 0, Iterator.class);
7117      *         // body type signature (V T A...), internal loop types (I V A...)
7118      *         step = swapArguments(body, 0, 1);  // swap V <-> T
7119      *     }
7120      *     if (startIter == null)  startIter = MH_getIter;
7121      *     MethodHandle[]
7122      *         iterVar    = { startIter, null, MH_hasNext, retv }, // it = iterator; while (it.hasNext())
7123      *         bodyClause = { init, filterArguments(step, 0, nextVal) };  // v = body(v, t, a)
7124      *     return loop(iterVar, bodyClause);
7125      * }
7126      * }</pre></blockquote>
7127      *
7128      * @param iterator an optional handle to return the iterator to start the loop.
7129      *                 If non-{@code null}, the handle must return {@link java.util.Iterator} or a subtype.
7130      *                 See above for other constraints.
7131      * @param init optional initializer, providing the initial value of the loop variable.
7132      *             May be {@code null}, implying a default initial value.  See above for other constraints.
7133      * @param body body of the loop, which may not be {@code null}.
7134      *             It controls the loop parameters and result type in the standard case (see above for details).
7135      *             It must accept its own return type (if non-void) plus a {@code T} parameter (for the iterated values),
7136      *             and may accept any number of additional types.
7137      *             See above for other constraints.
7138      *
7139      * @return a method handle embodying the iteration loop functionality.
7140      * @throws NullPointerException if the {@code body} handle is {@code null}.
7141      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if any argument violates the above requirements.
7142      *
7143      * @since 9
7144      */
7145     public static MethodHandle iteratedLoop(MethodHandle iterator, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
7146         Class<?> iterableType = iteratedLoopChecks(iterator, init, body);
7147         Class<?> returnType = body.type().returnType();
7148         MethodHandle hasNext = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_iteratePred);
7149         MethodHandle nextRaw = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_iterateNext);
7150         MethodHandle startIter;
7151         MethodHandle nextVal;
7152         {
7153             MethodType iteratorType;
7154             if (iterator == null) {
7155                 // derive argument type from body, if available, else use Iterable
7156                 startIter = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_initIterator);
7157                 iteratorType = startIter.type().changeParameterType(0, iterableType);
7158             } else {
7159                 // force return type to the internal iterator class
7160                 iteratorType = iterator.type().changeReturnType(Iterator.class);
7161                 startIter = iterator;
7162             }
7163             Class<?> ttype = body.type().parameterType(returnType == void.class ? 0 : 1);
7164             MethodType nextValType = nextRaw.type().changeReturnType(ttype);
7165 
7166             // perform the asType transforms under an exception transformer, as per spec.:
7167             try {
7168                 startIter = startIter.asType(iteratorType);
7169                 nextVal = nextRaw.asType(nextValType);
7170             } catch (WrongMethodTypeException ex) {
7171                 throw new IllegalArgumentException(ex);
7172             }
7173         }
7174 
7175         MethodHandle retv = null, step = body;
7176         if (returnType != void.class) {
7177             // the simple thing first:  in (I V A...), drop the I to get V
7178             retv = dropArguments(identity(returnType), 0, Iterator.class);
7179             // body type signature (V T A...), internal loop types (I V A...)
7180             step = swapArguments(body, 0, 1);  // swap V <-> T
7181         }
7182 
7183         MethodHandle[]
7184             iterVar    = { startIter, null, hasNext, retv },
7185             bodyClause = { init, filterArgument(step, 0, nextVal) };
7186         return loop(iterVar, bodyClause);
7187     }
7188 
7189     private static Class<?> iteratedLoopChecks(MethodHandle iterator, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
7190         Objects.requireNonNull(body);
7191         MethodType bodyType = body.type();
7192         Class<?> returnType = bodyType.returnType();
7193         List<Class<?>> internalParamList = bodyType.parameterList();
7194         // strip leading V value if present
7195         int vsize = (returnType == void.class ? 0 : 1);
7196         if (vsize != 0 && (internalParamList.size() == 0 || internalParamList.get(0) != returnType)) {
7197             // argument list has no "V" => error
7198             MethodType expected = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(0, returnType);
7199             throw misMatchedTypes("body function", bodyType, expected);
7200         } else if (internalParamList.size() <= vsize) {
7201             // missing T type => error
7202             MethodType expected = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(vsize, Object.class);
7203             throw misMatchedTypes("body function", bodyType, expected);
7204         }
7205         List<Class<?>> externalParamList = internalParamList.subList(vsize + 1, internalParamList.size());
7206         Class<?> iterableType = null;
7207         if (iterator != null) {
7208             // special case; if the body handle only declares V and T then
7209             // the external parameter list is obtained from iterator handle
7210             if (externalParamList.isEmpty()) {
7211                 externalParamList = iterator.type().parameterList();
7212             }
7213             MethodType itype = iterator.type();
7214             if (!Iterator.class.isAssignableFrom(itype.returnType())) {
7215                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("iteratedLoop first argument must have Iterator return type");
7216             }
7217             if (!itype.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, externalParamList)) {
7218                 MethodType expected = methodType(itype.returnType(), externalParamList);
7219                 throw misMatchedTypes("iterator parameters", itype, expected);
7220             }
7221         } else {
7222             if (externalParamList.isEmpty()) {
7223                 // special case; if the iterator handle is null and the body handle
7224                 // only declares V and T then the external parameter list consists
7225                 // of Iterable
7226                 externalParamList = Arrays.asList(Iterable.class);
7227                 iterableType = Iterable.class;
7228             } else {
7229                 // special case; if the iterator handle is null and the external
7230                 // parameter list is not empty then the first parameter must be
7231                 // assignable to Iterable
7232                 iterableType = externalParamList.get(0);
7233                 if (!Iterable.class.isAssignableFrom(iterableType)) {
7234                     throw newIllegalArgumentException(
7235                             "inferred first loop argument must inherit from Iterable: " + iterableType);
7236                 }
7237             }
7238         }
7239         if (init != null) {
7240             MethodType initType = init.type();
7241             if (initType.returnType() != returnType ||
7242                     !initType.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, externalParamList)) {
7243                 throw misMatchedTypes("loop initializer", initType, methodType(returnType, externalParamList));
7244             }
7245         }
7246         return iterableType;  // help the caller a bit
7247     }
7248 
7249     /*non-public*/
7250     static MethodHandle swapArguments(MethodHandle mh, int i, int j) {
7251         // there should be a better way to uncross my wires
7252         int arity = mh.type().parameterCount();
7253         int[] order = new int[arity];
7254         for (int k = 0; k < arity; k++)  order[k] = k;
7255         order[i] = j; order[j] = i;
7256         Class<?>[] types = mh.type().parameterArray();
7257         Class<?> ti = types[i]; types[i] = types[j]; types[j] = ti;
7258         MethodType swapType = methodType(mh.type().returnType(), types);
7259         return permuteArguments(mh, swapType, order);
7260     }
7261 
7262     /**
7263      * Makes a method handle that adapts a {@code target} method handle by wrapping it in a {@code try-finally} block.
7264      * Another method handle, {@code cleanup}, represents the functionality of the {@code finally} block. Any exception
7265      * thrown during the execution of the {@code target} handle will be passed to the {@code cleanup} handle. The
7266      * exception will be rethrown, unless {@code cleanup} handle throws an exception first.  The
7267      * value returned from the {@code cleanup} handle's execution will be the result of the execution of the
7268      * {@code try-finally} handle.
7269      * <p>
7270      * The {@code cleanup} handle will be passed one or two additional leading arguments.
7271      * The first is the exception thrown during the
7272      * execution of the {@code target} handle, or {@code null} if no exception was thrown.
7273      * The second is the result of the execution of the {@code target} handle, or, if it throws an exception,
7274      * a {@code null}, zero, or {@code false} value of the required type is supplied as a placeholder.
7275      * The second argument is not present if the {@code target} handle has a {@code void} return type.
7276      * (Note that, except for argument type conversions, combinators represent {@code void} values in parameter lists
7277      * by omitting the corresponding paradoxical arguments, not by inserting {@code null} or zero values.)
7278      * <p>
7279      * The {@code target} and {@code cleanup} handles must have the same corresponding argument and return types, except
7280      * that the {@code cleanup} handle may omit trailing arguments. Also, the {@code cleanup} handle must have one or
7281      * two extra leading parameters:<ul>
7282      * <li>a {@code Throwable}, which will carry the exception thrown by the {@code target} handle (if any); and
7283      * <li>a parameter of the same type as the return type of both {@code target} and {@code cleanup}, which will carry
7284      * the result from the execution of the {@code target} handle.
7285      * This parameter is not present if the {@code target} returns {@code void}.
7286      * </ul>
7287      * <p>
7288      * The pseudocode for the resulting adapter looks as follows. In the code, {@code V} represents the result type of
7289      * the {@code try/finally} construct; {@code A}/{@code a}, the types and values of arguments to the resulting
7290      * handle consumed by the cleanup; and {@code B}/{@code b}, those of arguments to the resulting handle discarded by
7291      * the cleanup.
7292      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
7293      * V target(A..., B...);
7294      * V cleanup(Throwable, V, A...);
7295      * V adapter(A... a, B... b) {
7296      *   V result = (zero value for V);
7297      *   Throwable throwable = null;
7298      *   try {
7299      *     result = target(a..., b...);
7300      *   } catch (Throwable t) {
7301      *     throwable = t;
7302      *     throw t;
7303      *   } finally {
7304      *     result = cleanup(throwable, result, a...);
7305      *   }
7306      *   return result;
7307      * }
7308      * }</pre></blockquote>
7309      * <p>
7310      * Note that the saved arguments ({@code a...} in the pseudocode) cannot
7311      * be modified by execution of the target, and so are passed unchanged
7312      * from the caller to the cleanup, if it is invoked.
7313      * <p>
7314      * The target and cleanup must return the same type, even if the cleanup
7315      * always throws.
7316      * To create such a throwing cleanup, compose the cleanup logic
7317      * with {@link #throwException throwException},
7318      * in order to create a method handle of the correct return type.
7319      * <p>
7320      * Note that {@code tryFinally} never converts exceptions into normal returns.
7321      * In rare cases where exceptions must be converted in that way, first wrap
7322      * the target with {@link #catchException(MethodHandle, Class, MethodHandle)}
7323      * to capture an outgoing exception, and then wrap with {@code tryFinally}.
7324      * <p>
7325      * It is recommended that the first parameter type of {@code cleanup} be
7326      * declared {@code Throwable} rather than a narrower subtype.  This ensures
7327      * {@code cleanup} will always be invoked with whatever exception that
7328      * {@code target} throws.  Declaring a narrower type may result in a
7329      * {@code ClassCastException} being thrown by the {@code try-finally}
7330      * handle if the type of the exception thrown by {@code target} is not
7331      * assignable to the first parameter type of {@code cleanup}.  Note that
7332      * various exception types of {@code VirtualMachineError},
7333      * {@code LinkageError}, and {@code RuntimeException} can in principle be
7334      * thrown by almost any kind of Java code, and a finally clause that
7335      * catches (say) only {@code IOException} would mask any of the others
7336      * behind a {@code ClassCastException}.
7337      *
7338      * @param target the handle whose execution is to be wrapped in a {@code try} block.
7339      * @param cleanup the handle that is invoked in the finally block.
7340      *
7341      * @return a method handle embodying the {@code try-finally} block composed of the two arguments.
7342      * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
7343      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code cleanup} does not accept
7344      *          the required leading arguments, or if the method handle types do
7345      *          not match in their return types and their
7346      *          corresponding trailing parameters
7347      *
7348      * @see MethodHandles#catchException(MethodHandle, Class, MethodHandle)
7349      * @since 9
7350      */
7351     public static MethodHandle tryFinally(MethodHandle target, MethodHandle cleanup) {
7352         List<Class<?>> targetParamTypes = target.type().parameterList();
7353         Class<?> rtype = target.type().returnType();
7354 
7355         tryFinallyChecks(target, cleanup);
7356 
7357         // Match parameter lists: if the cleanup has a shorter parameter list than the target, add ignored arguments.
7358         // The cleanup parameter list (minus the leading Throwable and result parameters) must be a sublist of the
7359         // target parameter list.
7360         cleanup = dropArgumentsToMatch(cleanup, (rtype == void.class ? 1 : 2), targetParamTypes, 0);
7361 
7362         // Ensure that the intrinsic type checks the instance thrown by the
7363         // target against the first parameter of cleanup
7364         cleanup = cleanup.asType(cleanup.type().changeParameterType(0, Throwable.class));
7365 
7366         // Use asFixedArity() to avoid unnecessary boxing of last argument for VarargsCollector case.
7367         return MethodHandleImpl.makeTryFinally(target.asFixedArity(), cleanup.asFixedArity(), rtype, targetParamTypes);
7368     }
7369 
7370     private static void tryFinallyChecks(MethodHandle target, MethodHandle cleanup) {
7371         Class<?> rtype = target.type().returnType();
7372         if (rtype != cleanup.type().returnType()) {
7373             throw misMatchedTypes("target and return types", cleanup.type().returnType(), rtype);
7374         }
7375         MethodType cleanupType = cleanup.type();
7376         if (!Throwable.class.isAssignableFrom(cleanupType.parameterType(0))) {
7377             throw misMatchedTypes("cleanup first argument and Throwable", cleanup.type(), Throwable.class);
7378         }
7379         if (rtype != void.class && cleanupType.parameterType(1) != rtype) {
7380             throw misMatchedTypes("cleanup second argument and target return type", cleanup.type(), rtype);
7381         }
7382         // The cleanup parameter list (minus the leading Throwable and result parameters) must be a sublist of the
7383         // target parameter list.
7384         int cleanupArgIndex = rtype == void.class ? 1 : 2;
7385         if (!cleanupType.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(cleanupArgIndex, target.type().parameterList())) {
7386             throw misMatchedTypes("cleanup parameters after (Throwable,result) and target parameter list prefix",
7387                     cleanup.type(), target.type());
7388         }
7389     }
7390 
7391 }
